Al-Jaʿd's Extreme Claim: Humans as True Creators
Al-Jaʿd's claim that God is not truly the Creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Abū ʿAbd Allāh al-Baṣrī (al-Jaʿd) went beyond previous Mu'tazila by denying that God is truly the Creator, instead attributing true creation solely to humans.

Core Idea
Al-Jaʿd claimed God is only metaphorically Creator; humans are the true creators.

The Mu'tazila deviation reached its peak with Abū ʿAbd Allāh al-Baṣrī, known as al-Jaʿd. He made an unprecedented statement: God is not the Creator in reality but only figuratively, while the human servant is the actual creator. This lesson examines this extreme position, which even polytheists had not dared to assert, and the Māturīdī response affirming God's transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Jaʿd's claim
Focus on the final part of the Arabic passage where al-Jaʿd's statement is recorded.
Note the phrase 'not a creator in truth, but metaphorically'.
2
Compare with earlier positions
This goes far beyond al-Jubbāʾī. Reflect on how language shifted from cautious terms to outright denial of God's creative attribute.
3
Understand the Māturīdī response
The passage ends with an exclamation of God's transcendence. This is the author's condemnation of such a view.
The formula 'exalted be God above what the wrongdoers say' is a standard refutation.

?
When you fail or sin, do you blame yourself as the ultimate cause, forgetting that God's permission and decree are involved? How would turning to God as the true agent change your repentance and humility?

Ash'ari View on Human Acts: Terminological Difference
Author explains Ash'ari position on human acts is terminological and points out a contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Ash'ari position on human acts is terminologically distinct from the Maturidi but not substantively different, and you will identify the internal contradiction in their terminology.

Core Idea
Ash'ari and Maturidi agree on the reality of human acts; their dispute is only about words.

This passage examines the relationship between the Ash'ari and Maturidi schools on the nature of human acts. The author argues that although Ash'aris use different terminology—calling the human act 'kasb' rather than 'fi'l'—the underlying doctrine is the same. However, he points out an inconsistency: the Ash'ari school itself uses the term 'fi'l' in the chapter title 'Creation of Servants' Acts'. This contradiction reveals that the dispute is merely verbal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and then the English translation. Pay attention to the key terms: kasb, fi'l, khalq.
Notice the opening bracket in the Arabic—it indicates an editorial insertion.
2
Identify the Ash'ari claim
The passage states that Ash'aris call the human act 'kasb' and refuse to call it 'fi'l' or 'khalq'. Note why this matters.
This is about terminology, not denial of human agency.
3
Analyze the contradiction
The author points out that al-Ash'ari and his followers themselves use the term 'af'āl' (acts) in the chapter title. Find this in the passage and understand why it is contradictory.
The contradiction is between their refusal and their own usage.
4
Draw the conclusion
The author concludes that the difference is only in expression, not in the reality of the doctrine. Reflect on what this means for understanding sectarian disputes.
This is a key insight: many theological debates are verbal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مذهب الأشاعرة قريب من الماتريدية] ثم الأشعرية إن وافقونا في حقيقة المذهب فقد زعمت أن ما هو مقدور العبد يسمى كسبًا ولا يسمى فعلاً له كما لا خلقًا، يسمى وهذا منه امتناع عن إطلاق ما أطلقه الله بقوله : ( وَافَعَلُوا الخير ) (۳) وغير ذلك من الآيات، وأطلق جميع أهل اللسان قولهم: فعل فلان كذا ، وفلان كريم الفعال، وأطلق هو وجميع المتكلمين، فإن الناس بأجمعهم يسمون هذا الباب باب خلق أفعال العباد كذا ذكر الأشعري في كتبه (٤) وكذا جميع أصحابه، والامتناع عن إطلاق ما أطلق هو بنفسه تناقض، وقع تبع الأشعري في هذا الرأي أبا عيسى محمد بن عيسى الملقب ببرغوث (۱) وهو في الحقيقة اختلاف في العبارة دون حقيقة المذهب.
The doctrine of the Ash'aris is close to the Maturidi. Then the Ash'aris, if they agree with us in the reality of the doctrine, they have claimed that what is within the servant's power is called 'kasb' and not called 'fi'l' for him, just as it is not called 'khalq'. This is a refusal to apply what Allah applied in His saying: 'and do good' and other verses. And all people of the tongue have applied their saying: 'so-and-so did such-and-such', and 'so-and-so is generous in doing'. And he (al-Ash'ari) and all the theologians apply that, for all people call this chapter 'the chapter on the creation of the acts of servants'. Thus mentioned al-Ash'ari in his books, and likewise all his followers. And refusal to apply what he himself applied is a contradiction that occurred. Al-Ash'ari followed in this opinion Abu 'Isa Muhammad ibn 'Isa known as Barghuth, and it is in reality a difference in expression, not in the reality of the doctrine.
Source pages p. 852

Commentary
This passage addresses the relationship between the Maturidi and Ash'ari schools on human acts. The author first notes that the Ash'ari school is close to the Maturidi in the reality of the doctrine. Then he critiques that the Ash'aris claim that what is within the servant's power is called 'kasb' (acquisition) and not called 'fi'l' (act), nor do they attribute 'khalq' (creation) to the servant. He argues this is a refusal to use the same term Allah Himself used in the Quran, such as 'wa if'alū al-khayr' (and do good). Moreover, all Arabic speakers use the term 'fi'l' for human actions. Al-Ash'ari himself and his followers refer to this whole topic as 'Bāb Khalq Afʿāl al-ʿIbād' (Chapter on Creation of Servants' Acts), which includes the word 'afʿāl' (acts). Thus, by refusing to call the servant's act 'fi'l' in one context but then using the same word for the topic title, they contradict themselves. However, the author concludes that this is ultimately a difference in expression rather than a difference in the actual doctrine. He also notes that al-Ash'ari followed Abu Isa Muhammad ibn Isa al-Barghuth in this view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Ash'aris completely deny human agency and believe humans have no role in their actions.
Correction: The author shows that Ash'aris only differ in terminology; they still affirm human acquisition (kasb) and agree with Maturidis on the reality of human acts.

Checkpoint
What contradiction does the author point out in the Ash'ari position?
A) They call human acts 'khalq' while denying 'fi'l'
B) They refuse to use 'fi'l' for human acts but themselves call the topic 'خلق أفعال العباد'
C) They deny human ability entirely
D) They agree with Maturidis on everything

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari-Maturidi difference on human acts is a dispute over expressions, not over the substance of the doctrine.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever clung to a specific word or label in a disagreement while actually agreeing on the substance? How did that affect the relationship? Reflect on a real example from your life—what would it take for you to let go of that word for the sake of unity?
?
This lesson shows that even a great scholar like al-Ash'ari can fall into a verbal contradiction. In your own study or discussions of Islam, are you more focused on the reality of a teaching or on the terminology used to describe it? Think of a topic where you might be overemphasizing words. What practical step will you take to prioritize substance over form?
?
When you differ with someone on a religious matter, do you pause to ask if the disagreement is truly about the reality or only about how it is expressed? Name a specific disagreement you have right now—is it possible that you both actually agree on the core issue but are stuck on words? What would it cost you to admit that?

The Absurdity of Attributing All Actions to God
Nasafi presents a reductio ad absurdum of the Jabriyya view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's reductio ad absurdum argument against the Jabriyya, showing that if God alone creates all actions, then commands, prohibitions, and recompense become incoherent.

Core Idea
If God does everything, He would be commanding and rewarding Himself.

In debating the Jabriyya, Nasafi first turns to the logical consequences of their position. He argues that if every human action is created by God alone, then the very concepts of divine command, prohibition, reward, and punishment would collapse into absurdity. The following passage presents this reductio ad absurdum.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice how Nasafi builds his argument step by step.
Pay attention to the repetition of 'لا قوة إلا بالله' as a refrain.
2
Identify the three absurdities
The passage lists three main absurdities: God commanding Himself, God rewarding/punishing Himself, and attributing servant-like names to God. Identify each one.
3
Understand the reductio structure
Nasafi shows that if the Jabriyya premise (all actions from God) is accepted, then these absurdities follow. Since the consequences are impossible, the premise must be false.
This is a standard theological argument style.
4
Reflect on revelation and reason
The passage concludes that the Jabriyya view is rejected by both divine revelation (سمع) and human reason (عقل). Ask yourself why both are needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفواحش والمناكير ، وأنه المأمور المنهى المثاب المعاقب، فبطل أن يكون الفعل من هذه الوجوه له ولا قوة إلا بالله وأيضا أن الله تعالى إنما وعد الثواب لمن أطاعه الدنيا والعقاب لمن عصاه فإذا كان الأمران فعله فإذا هو المجزي بما ذكر، وإذا كان الثواب والعقاب حقيقة فالائتمار والانتهاء كذلك، ولا قوة إلا بالله تعالى وكذلك في العقل محال أن يأمر أحد نفسه أو يطيعه أو يعصيه، ومحال تسمية الله تعالى عبدًا ذليلاً مطيعا عاصيًا سفيهًا جائراً، وقد سمى الله تعالى بهذا كله أولئك الذين أمرهم ونهاهم، فإذا صارت هذه الأسماء في التحقيق له فيكون هو الرب وهو العبد وهو الخالق والمخلوق ولا غيره ثُمَّ، وذلك مدفوع في السمع والعقل جميعًا، ولا قوة إلا بالله وأيضا أن كل حد يعلم من نفسه أنه مختار لما يفعله، وأنه فاعل كاسب فلو جاز صرف مثله عما هو طريق العلم به الحس أو إبطاله فحق العلم بجميع العالم مثله، وذلك قول مهجور، ومثله قول أهل الجبر، وهذا قول تغني الحكاية عن الإطناب فيه لانقراض الجبرية عن آخرهم وارتفاع مقالتهم، ولما ليس لهذا القول معنى تكلم عليه صاحبه إذ هو ينفي عن نفسه حقيقة كل قول وفعل، وإذا انتفى بطل القول، وبه يناظر ويحاج، فزال الذي يكون به الحجاج واضمحل.
The obscenities and abominations, and that He is the commanded, forbidden, rewarded, punished. So it is invalid that the action in these respects is from Him, and there is no power except with Allah. And also that Allah Almighty surely promised reward in this world to whoever obeys Him and punishment to whoever disobeys Him. If both matters are His action, then He is the one who recompenses what was mentioned. And if reward and punishment are real, then obeying commands and refraining from prohibitions are likewise, and there is no power except with Allah Almighty. And likewise, it is impossible in reason for a person to command himself or obey him or disobey him. And it is impossible to call Allah Almighty a humble servant, obedient, disobedient, foolish, or unjust. Yet Allah Almighty has called by all these those whom He commanded and forbade. So if these names become in reality attributed to Him, then He would be the Lord and the servant, the Creator and the created, and none other. That is rejected by both revelation and reason, and there is no power except with Allah. And also that every individual knows from himself that he is free in what he does, and that he is an acquirer and doer. So if it were permissible to divert someone like this from what is the path of knowledge by sense or to nullify it, then the knowledge of the entire world would be like it. That is an abandoned statement, and similar is the statement of the proponents of compulsion (ahl al-jabr). This statement is such that the narration suffices without elaboration due to the extinction of the Jabriyya to the last of them and the elevation of their doctrine. And since this statement has no meaning, its proponent spoke about it, for he negates from himself the reality of every statement and action. And when it is negated, the statement becomes invalid, and with it he argues and debates, so that by which debate occurs vanishes and disappears.
Source pages p. 854

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Jabriyya position that all actions are created by God and humans have no real agency. Nasafi argues that if all actions were from God, then the very concepts of command, prohibition, reward, and punishment would become absurd because they would all revert to God Himself. He notes that God commands and forbids humans, rewards obedience and punishes disobedience. If God were the sole agent of those actions, then He would be commanding Himself, forbidding Himself, rewarding Himself, and punishing Himself. This is impossible. Similarly, it is impossible in reason for a person to command himself or obey himself in a meaningful sense. Moreover, it is impossible to attribute to God the names that apply to servants such as disobedient, foolish, etc. Yet God Himself uses these names for those He commands. If these names applied to God, He would be everything contradictory. This is rejected by both revelation and reason. Additionally, every person knows from his own experience that he has choice and is an acquirer (kasb) of his actions. To deny this self-evident knowledge would undermine all knowledge. Thus the Jabriyya position is abandoned and its proponents are extinct.

Key Terms
جبرية
جبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Nasafi is arguing against any divine involvement in human actions.
Correction: Nasafi only refutes the extreme Jabriyya view; he affirms human agency while upholding divine sovereignty (e.g., kasb).

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what would be the consequence if God were the sole agent of all human actions?
A) God would be just in commanding
B) God would be commanding Himself
C) Humans would be free
D) Reward and punishment would be meaningless

Key Takeaway
If God were the doer of all actions, then commands, prohibitions, rewards, and punishments would be directed to God Himself, which is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you ever catch yourself feeling as though it was 'written' or 'destined' in a way that absolves you of responsibility? How does Nasafi's argument shatter that excuse?
?
If you truly believe that God rewards you for your obedience and punishes you for your disobedience, what does that demand from you in the next moment you are tempted to sin?
?
Consider a specific wrong you have done. Can you honestly say you had no choice, or does this lesson expose a subtle way you may have been using the doctrine of predestination to avoid repentance? What are you going to do about it today?

The Self-Evident Knowledge of Human Agency
Nasafi argues from self-awareness and sense perception to affirm human agency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's argument from self-awareness and sense perception to refute the Jabriyya, and why their position has become extinct.

Core Idea
Every person knows from within that he chooses and acquires his actions.

After presenting the absurd consequences of the Jabriyya view, Nasafi turns to a direct argument based on human self-knowledge. He argues that every person is aware of his own free choice and acquisition of actions, and to deny this would undermine all knowledge based on sense perception. He then concludes that the Jabriyya position is so untenable that it has died out.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice how Nasafi shifts from external arguments to an internal, self-evident one.
2
Understand the premise of self-knowledge
Nasafi states that every individual knows from himself that he is free in his actions (مختار) and that he is an acquirer and doer (فاعل كاسب). This is claimed as a universal, self-evident truth.
This is a key concept in Maturidi kalam: kasb (acquisition).
3
Grasp the reductio on knowledge
If this self-evident knowledge can be denied, then all knowledge derived from sense perception can be denied, leading to skepticism. Thus the Jabriyya position is an abandoned statement.
4
Note the historical conclusion
Nasafi remarks that the Jabriyya have become extinct and their doctrine is no longer debated, because it negates the very reality of speech and action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفواحش والمناكير ، وأنه المأمور المنهى المثاب المعاقب، فبطل أن يكون الفعل من هذه الوجوه له ولا قوة إلا بالله وأيضا أن الله تعالى إنما وعد الثواب لمن أطاعه الدنيا والعقاب لمن عصاه فإذا كان الأمران فعله فإذا هو المجزي بما ذكر، وإذا كان الثواب والعقاب حقيقة فالائتمار والانتهاء كذلك، ولا قوة إلا بالله تعالى وكذلك في العقل محال أن يأمر أحد نفسه أو يطيعه أو يعصيه، ومحال تسمية الله تعالى عبدًا ذليلاً مطيعا عاصيًا سفيهًا جائراً، وقد سمى الله تعالى بهذا كله أولئك الذين أمرهم ونهاهم، فإذا صارت هذه الأسماء في التحقيق له فيكون هو الرب وهو العبد وهو الخالق والمخلوق ولا غيره ثُمَّ، وذلك مدفوع في السمع والعقل جميعًا، ولا قوة إلا بالله وأيضا أن كل حد يعلم من نفسه أنه مختار لما يفعله، وأنه فاعل كاسب فلو جاز صرف مثله عما هو طريق العلم به الحس أو إبطاله فحق العلم بجميع العالم مثله، وذلك قول مهجور، ومثله قول أهل الجبر، وهذا قول تغني الحكاية عن الإطناب فيه لانقراض الجبرية عن آخرهم وارتفاع مقالتهم، ولما ليس لهذا القول معنى تكلم عليه صاحبه إذ هو ينفي عن نفسه حقيقة كل قول وفعل، وإذا انتفى بطل القول، وبه يناظر ويحاج، فزال الذي يكون به الحجاج واضمحل.
The obscenities and abominations, and that He is the commanded, forbidden, rewarded, punished. So it is invalid that the action in these respects is from Him, and there is no power except with Allah. And also that Allah Almighty surely promised reward in this world to whoever obeys Him and punishment to whoever disobeys Him. If both matters are His action, then He is the one who recompenses what was mentioned. And if reward and punishment are real, then obeying commands and refraining from prohibitions are likewise, and there is no power except with Allah Almighty. And likewise, it is impossible in reason for a person to command himself or obey him or disobey him. And it is impossible to call Allah Almighty a humble servant, obedient, disobedient, foolish, or unjust. Yet Allah Almighty has called by all these those whom He commanded and forbade. So if these names become in reality attributed to Him, then He would be the Lord and the servant, the Creator and the created, and none other. That is rejected by both revelation and reason, and there is no power except with Allah. And also that every individual knows from himself that he is free in what he does, and that he is an acquirer and doer. So if it were permissible to divert someone like this from what is the path of knowledge by sense or to nullify it, then the knowledge of the entire world would be like it. That is an abandoned statement, and similar is the statement of the proponents of compulsion (ahl al-jabr). This statement is such that the narration suffices without elaboration due to the extinction of the Jabriyya to the last of them and the elevation of their doctrine. And since this statement has no meaning, its proponent spoke about it, for he negates from himself the reality of every statement and action. And when it is negated, the statement becomes invalid, and with it he argues and debates, so that by which debate occurs vanishes and disappears.
Source pages p. 854

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Jabriyya position that all actions are created by God and humans have no real agency. Nasafi argues that if all actions were from God, then the very concepts of command, prohibition, reward, and punishment would become absurd because they would all revert to God Himself. He notes that God commands and forbids humans, rewards obedience and punishes disobedience. If God were the sole agent of those actions, then He would be commanding Himself, forbidding Himself, rewarding Himself, and punishing Himself. This is impossible. Similarly, it is impossible in reason for a person to command himself or obey himself in a meaningful sense. Moreover, it is impossible to attribute to God the names that apply to servants such as disobedient, foolish, etc. Yet God Himself uses these names for those He commands. If these names applied to God, He would be everything contradictory. This is rejected by both revelation and reason. Additionally, every person knows from his own experience that he has choice and is an acquirer (kasb) of his actions. To deny this self-evident knowledge would undermine all knowledge. Thus the Jabriyya position is abandoned and its proponents are extinct.

Key Terms
جبرية
جبر
الكسب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Nasafi teaches that humans create their own actions independently of God.
Correction: Nasafi teaches acquisition (kasb): humans choose and acquire actions, but Allah creates them.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what does every person know from himself?
A) That Allah controls all actions
B) That he is free and an acquirer
C) That knowledge is impossible
D) That the Jabriyya are correct

Key Takeaway
Human self-awareness of choice and acquisition is a bedrock of knowledge that refutes the Jabriyya, and their position has become extinct.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what areas of your life do you subtly act as if your choices are not real, blaming circumstances or fate? How does Nasafi's argument that you know yourself to be free challenge you to take full responsibility for your actions today?
?
If you deny your own agency, as the Jabriyya did, you negate the reality of every statement and action. Have you ever used theological fatalism as an excuse to avoid making a difficult decision? What would it mean for you to embrace the self-evident knowledge that you are indeed the acquirer of your deeds?
?
Nasafi says this doctrine is so self-defeating that it vanished. Are there any beliefs you hold that, if fully lived out, would contradict your own experience of being a responsible moral agent? Will you re-examine them?

Mu'tazila Proof from 'Best of Creators'
Mu'tazila proof from Qur'anic verse using comparative phrase.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila's argument that the Qur'anic phrase 'best of creators' implies the existence of other creators besides Allah.

Core Idea
A comparison like 'best of creators' only makes sense if there are multiple creators.

The Mu'tazila were known for using rational arguments to defend human free will. One of their key proofs comes directly from the Qur'an, in the verse that calls Allah 'the best of creators.' At first glance, this might seem to affirm that Allah is the only creator — but the Mu'tazila read it differently. Let's examine their reasoning carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazila's argument
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the Mu'tazila's line of reasoning from the verse.
Pay attention to the analogy they draw with phrases like 'most skilled of writers.'
2
Identify the logical structure
The argument uses a comparison (superlative) to imply the existence of others. Compare with the impossibility of 'greatest of gods.'
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider how this argument supports the Mu'tazila position that humans are creators of their own actions.
This is a foundational proof in the debate on free will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الكلام بيننا وبين المعتزلة فنبدأ ببيان ما لهم من الشبه فنقول: إنهم يحتجون من كتاب الله تعالى كقوله تعالى : فَتَبَارَكَ اللَّهُ أَحْسَنُ الْخَلِقِينَ في الآية دلالة كون غيره خالقا لأن إطلاق ذلك يوجب أن له تعالى مزية على كل خالق كما يقال : فلان أحذق الكتاب وأجودهم خطا . ألا ترى أن القول بأنه تعالى أكبر الآلهة محال لاستحالة ثبوت الإلهية لغيره، وهاهنا لما أطلق هذا دل أن غيره خالق. ويتعلقون أيضا بالأمر والنهي والوعد والوعيد الثابتة من الله تعالى للناس في أفعال مختلفة، ولو كان الله تعالى هو الذي تولى تخليق أفعالهم وإيجادها لصار أمراً نفسه ناهيًا إياه واعدًا إياه موعدًا إياه لأنه هو الذي تولى إيجادها، فكان هو المؤمن والكافر والمطيع والعاص، وذا محال من تفوه به يحكم بانسلاخه عن الدين. وكذا الذم والمدح على ما يذم ويمدح عليه من الأفعال يكونان راجعين إليه لأن الموجد بذلك أولى ممن ليس بموجد. وكذا التعذيب والإثابة يحصلان على فعل نفسه وهما مقابلان بالفعل، فينبغي أن يكون الله تعالى هو المعاقب المثاب لا العبد، والقول به كفر.
As for the discussion between us and the Mu'tazila, we begin by clarifying what proofs they have. We say: They argue from the Book of Allah Almighty, such as His statement: 'So blessed is Allah, the best of creators.' In the verse is an indication that others besides Him are creators, because the use of this expression necessitates that He Almighty has superiority over every creator, just as it is said: 'So-and-so is the most skilled of the writers and the finest of them in handwriting.' Do you not see that the statement that He Almighty is the greatest of the gods is impossible due to the impossibility of divinity existing for others? Here, since He used this expression, it indicates that others besides Him are creators. They also rely on command and prohibition and promise and threat established from Allah Almighty for people concerning different actions. If Allah Almighty were the one who undertook the creation and bringing into existence of their actions, He would become one commanding Himself, forbidding Himself, promising Himself, threatening Himself, because He is the one who undertook their existence. So He would be the believer and the disbeliever, the obedient and the disobedient. That is impossible; whoever utters it is judged to have stripped himself of religion. Likewise, blame and praise concerning the actions for which one is blamed or praised would revert to Him, because the one who brings them into existence is more entitled to them than one who does not. Likewise, punishment and reward occur for His own action, and they are counterparts to the action, so it should be that Allah Almighty is the one punished and rewarded, not the servant, and saying that is disbelief.
Source pages p. 854

Commentary
This passage presents two of the Mu'tazila's proofs for human free will. The first proof is from the Qur'anic verse "فاتبارك الله أحسن الخالقين" (Blessed is Allah, the best of creators). The Mu'tazila argue that the phrase 'best of creators' implies that there are other creators besides Allah, otherwise the comparison would be meaningless. Just as one says 'most skilled of writers' implies multiple writers, so here 'best of creators' implies multiple creators. They compare it to the phrase 'greatest of gods' which is impossible because there are no other gods. Thus the verse indicates that humans create their own actions. The second proof is from the existence of command, prohibition, promise, and threat in the Qur'an. If God were the sole creator of human actions, then He would be commanding and forbidding Himself, promising and threatening Himself. This would lead to absurdities such as God being the believer and the disbeliever, the obedient and the disobedient. Moreover, blame and praise for actions would revert to God, and reward and punishment would be for His own action. All of this is impossible and tantamount to disbelief.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
خلق
أحسن الخالقين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'best of creators' only affirms that Allah is the sole creator and does not imply others.
Correction: The Mu'tazila argue that the comparative form necessarily implies the existence of others, just as 'most skilled writer' implies other writers.

Checkpoint
What analogy do the Mu'tazila use to support their argument from 'best of creators'?
A) The statement 'greatest of gods' is impossible
B) The phrase 'most skilled of writers' implies multiple writers
C) The verse itself is ambiguous
D) Allah cannot be compared to anything

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila argue that the Qur'anic phrase 'best of creators' logically requires the existence of other creators, supporting human free will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you achieve something, do you honestly feel that you are the sole creator of that success, or do you acknowledge Allah as the ultimate Creator? How often do you catch yourself forgetting the latter?
?
If the Mu'tazila were wrong in their reasoning, what does that tell you about your own tendency to lean on human logic when interpreting divine words? Where in your life today might you be trusting your own understanding over clear revelation?
?
Think of a time you judged someone for their actions, feeling they were entirely responsible. Does this lesson challenge that assumption? Will you now look at others' deeds as also created by Allah, balancing justice with mercy?

Mu'tazila Proof from Command and Prohibition
Mu'tazila proof from command, prohibition, promise, threat leading to absurdity if God creates all actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila argument that if God were the sole creator of human actions, command, prohibition, promise, and threat would become absurd.

Core Idea
If God creates all actions, then He commands and forbids Himself.

The Mu'tazila present a second powerful argument based on the presence of divine commands, prohibitions, promises, and threats in the Qur'an. If God were the direct creator of every human action, then these injunctions would apply to God Himself, leading to unacceptable conclusions. Let's trace their reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the Mu'tazila's logical chain.
Notice the consequences they derive: God would be commanding Himself, etc.
2
Trace the implications
Follow the argument: if God creates all actions, then the actions commanded and prohibited are God's own actions. This leads to absurdities like God being the believer and the disbeliever.
3
Consider the conclusion
The Mu'tazila conclude that humans must be the creators of their own actions, otherwise reward and punishment would be unjust.
This is a key argument for human responsibility.

Source Text

The Mu'tazila argue that the phrase 'best of creators' implies that there are other creators besides Allah, otherwise the comparison would be meaningless. Nasafi Exposes Contradiction in Opponents' Verse Interpretation
Nasafi criticizes opponents' inconsistent use of Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi exposes the contradictory way his opponents apply Quranic verses to deny the creation of human acts while rejecting the Maturidi use of other verses.

Core Idea
Contradiction: they use verses about false claims to deny creation, but reject our verse based on same logic.

Nasafi turns the tables on his opponents by highlighting their inconsistency. They cite verses like 'Allah has not made Bahirah nor Sa'ibah' to argue that God does not create human acts, yet when the Maturidis use the verse 'Creator of all things,' they object that the dispute was not contemporary. Nasafi shows this double standard is pure contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp Nasafi's argument.
2
Identify the opponent's claim
Note how opponents use Quran 3:78 and 5:103 to deny that God creates human acts.
3
Understand Nasafi's refutation
See how he points out the contradiction: they apply these verses despite no contemporary dispute on creation, but reject our verse for the same reason.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider the principle: consistency in interpreting scripture is crucial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعجب من وقاحتهم حيث يتعلقون في المسألة بقوله : وَإِنَّ مِنْهُمْ لَفَرِيقًا يَلْوُونَ أَلْسِنَتَهُم بِالْكِتَابِ لِتَحْسَبُوهُ مِنَ الْكِتَابِ وَمَا هُوَ مِنَ الْكِتَابِ وَيَقُولُونَ هُوَ مِنْ عِندِ اللَّهِ وَمَا هُوَ مِنْ عِندِ اللَّهِ وقالوا : نفى أن يكون ليهم ألسنتهم من عند الله، وكذا قوله تعالى: مَا جَعَلَ اللَّهُ مِن بَحِيرَةٍ وَلَا سَائِبَةٍ الآية، ويتعلقون به في نفي خلق الأفعال مع أن الخصوم كانوا يدعون ذلك شرعًا، والآية وردت لبيان أنها ليست بمشروعة من الله تعالى ولا يبالون من صرف الآية إلى أفعال العباد وإن لم تكن المنازعة واقعة في ذلك الزمان في تخليقها، ثم يصرفون الآية التي نتعلق بها نحن إلى غير الأفعال لانعدام المنازعة فيها في ذلك الزمان، وهذا هو عين التناقض وغاية الوقاحة والتحكم على الكتاب بآرائهم الفاسدة - عصمنا الله تعالى عن ذلك.
And amazing is their impudence when they cling in this issue to His saying: 'Indeed, among them is a party who twist their tongues with the Book that you may think it is from the Book, but it is not from the Book, and they say it is from Allah, but it is not from Allah.' They said: He denied that their twisting of their tongues is from Allah. And likewise His saying, the Exalted: 'Allah has not made Bahirah nor Sa'ibah' [5:103] etc. They cling to it in denying the creation of acts, while the opponents used to claim that as law, and the verse was revealed to show that it is not legislated by Allah. And they do not care to divert the verse to the acts of servants even though the dispute over their creation was not occurring in that time. Then they divert the verse that we cling to to other than acts because of the absence of dispute over them in that time. And this is clear contradiction and utmost impudence and imposition upon the Book with their corrupt opinions—may Allah protect us from that.
Source pages p. 867

Commentary
Nasafi expresses astonishment at the impudence of his opponents. They cite verses like 'Indeed, among them is a party who twist their tongues with the Book' (Quran 3:78) and 'Allah has not made Bahirah nor Sa'ibah' (Quran 5:103) to argue that God does not create human acts, because these verses deny that certain things come from God. But these verses are about false claims of divine legislation, not about the creation of acts. The opponents apply these verses to human acts even though the dispute about creation of acts was not contemporary, yet they reject our use of the verse 'Creator of all things' for acts on the grounds that the dispute was not contemporary. This is a blatant contradiction and an arbitrary imposition on the Quran.

Key Terms
وقاحة
التناقض
التحكم
البحيرة
السائبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that verses like 'Allah has not made Bahirah nor Sa'ibah' prove that God does not create human acts because they deny that certain things come from God.
Correction: These verses are about false claims of divine legislation, not about the creation of human acts. They deny that those practices are divinely mandated, not that they exist as created events.

Checkpoint
What contradiction does Nasafi point out in the opponents' use of Quranic verses?
A) They use verses about false claims to deny creation of acts, but reject our verse because the dispute was not contemporary, while they themselves use verses not directly about creation.
B) They accept our verse but misinterpret it.
C) They do not use any verses.
D) They agree the verse applies to acts.

Key Takeaway
Consistency in interpreting scripture is essential; conflicting applications reveal flawed methodology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever twisted a Quranic verse to justify a personal opinion, just as Nasafi accuses his opponents of doing? What would it take for you to submit to the text even when it contradicts your desires?
?
When you read the Quran, do you let the context guide your understanding, or do you impose your own agenda? Think of a specific instance where you ignored context—how can you correct that?
?
Nasafi calls the opponents' inconsistency 'utmost impudence.' Are you consistent in applying Islamic teachings across all areas of your life, or do you make exceptions for convenience? What area requires urgent consistency from you today?

Refuting the Mu'tazila on 'Ahsan al-Khaliqin'
Al-Nasafi refutes Mu'tazila use of verse by linguistic distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazila's claim that the verse 'Ahsan al-khaliqin' proves human creative power by distinguishing different meanings of 'khaliq'.

Core Idea
The word 'khaliq' can mean 'estimator' or 'shaper', not only 'creator'.

The Mu'tazila often cited the Qur'anic verse 'So blessed be Allah, the best of creators' (al-Mu'minun 23:14) to argue that humans too can be called creators in a real sense. Al-Nasafi, however, points out that even the early Mu'tazila agreed that only Allah is truly a creator. He then shows that the term 'khalq' in Arabic can refer to estimation and formation, not just invention from nothing, thereby undermining the Mu'tazilite argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Notice how Al-Nasafi structures his refutation.
The passage ends with a colon before a line of poetry; for this lesson we focus on the argument leading up to it.
2
Identify the two Mu'tazila groups
The passage mentions 'early Basrans and all Baghdadis' and 'later Basrans'. Understand their different positions. The early group agrees with Ahl al-Sunnah; the later group permits calling humans 'khaliq'.
3
Understand the key linguistic point
Al-Nasafi argues that 'khalq' can mean taqdir (estimation) and taswir (formation) without ikhtira' (invention) and ijad (origination). This allows calling a human 'khaliq' metaphorically, not as a true creator.
This is the core refutation against the later Basrans.
4
See how this refutes the verse citation
Even if the later Basrans use the verse 'Ahsan al-khaliqin', the verse can be understood as 'best of estimators/shaper', not 'best of originators'. Thus it does not prove human creation ex nihilo.
5
Reflect on the theological implication
This argument preserves the unique creative power of Allah. Only Allah creates from nothing; human 'creation' is merely shaping or estimating. This aligns with the Ahl al-Sunnah position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مناقشة في آية (فتبارك الله أحسن الخالقين): ثم المتعلق من أوائل البصرية وجميع البغدادية منهم بقوله تعالى: ﴿ أَحْسَنُ الْخَالِقِينَ ﴾ ليس بصحيح لمساعدتهم إيانا على أن من سوى الله تعالى ليس بخالق ويستحيل وصف من سواه به، ولو تعلق بذلك متأخرو أهل البصرة المجوزون ذلك يقال لهم: الخلق يذكر ويراد به التقدير والتصوير دون الاختراع والإيجاد، وعلى هذا التقدير يجوز أن يسمى العبد خالقا قال قائلهم:
Discussion of the verse 'So blessed be Allah, the best of creators' (al-Mu'minun 23:14). Then the attachment of the early Basrans and all the Baghdadis among them to His statement 'the best of creators' is not correct, because they agree with us that other than Allah is not a creator and it is impossible to describe anyone other than Him with it. And if the later Basrans who permit that cling to it, it is said to them: 'al-khalq' is mentioned and meant by it estimation (taqdir) and formation (taswir) without invention (ikhtira') and origination (ijad). On this estimation, it is permissible to call the servant a creator, as their poet said:

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila who use the verse 'So blessed be Allah, the best of creators' (Surah al-Mu'minun 23:14) to argue that humans can be called creators in the same sense as God. Al-Nasafi points out that the early Basrans and Baghdadis among the Mu'tazila actually agree with the Ahl al-Sunnah that no one other than Allah is a creator in the true sense (invention and origination from nothing). If later Basrans permit calling humans creators, they are refuted by noting that the word 'khalq' in Arabic can mean 'estimation' (taqdir) and 'formation' (taswir), not necessarily 'invention' (ikhtira') and 'origination' (ijad). In this metaphorical sense, a human can be called a creator, as the poet said (the line is cut off). Thus the verse does not support their claim that humans have genuine creative power.

Nasafi's Refutation of Mu'tazilite Interpretation of Creation Verse
Imam Nasafi refutes Mu'tazilite interpretation of a Quranic verse on creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazilite interpretation of a Quranic verse by using their own principle that act and object are one.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazilite principle of act-object unity actually undermines their interpretation of creation.

Imam Nasafi presents a sharp refutation of a Mu'tazilite interpretation of a Quranic verse about creation. He first dismisses a weak answer that tries to reconcile the verse's ambiguous wording, then delivers a knockout argument using the Mu'tazilites' own principle that act and object are identical. This passage shows how internal inconsistency can be used to refute a theological position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the flow of the argument from the weak answer to the stronger refutation.
2
Identify the two refutations
Find the first answer given by some mutakallimūn and Nasafi's judgment of it. Then find the second, stronger refutation based on the Mu'tazilite principle that act and object are one.
The first refutation is described as weak; the second is the main point.
3
Understand the Mu'tazilite principle
The Mu'tazilites hold that act (fi'l) and object (maf'ūl) are one. How does this apply to idols? Why does it break their interpretation?
The idol is not an action, so it cannot be the object of the verb if act and object are identical.
4
Contrast with the carving verse
Notice how Nasafi uses the verse 'Do you worship what you carve?' to show that carving is distinct from the carved object, unlike the idol situation.
This contrast highlights the inconsistency in the Mu'tazilite position.
5
Reflect on the refutation's strength
Why is this refutation effective? Because it uses the opponent's own premises to defeat their argument.
This is a classic dialectical technique.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعض المتكلمين أجاب أن الآية لما احتملت الأمرين أعني أن هذه اللفظة لما كانت تذكر ويراد بها المعمول، وتذكر ويراد بها العمل حملت عليهما جميعًا، ولكن فيه وهاء لما فيه من جعل المشترك مشتملاً وهو غير سديد. ثم مما يبطل التأويل على أصل المعتزلة أن عندهم الفعل والمفعول واحد فكان العمل والمعمول واحدًا، والصنم ليس بعمل للعهد فلا يكون معموله، فأما الفعل في الصنم فهو فعل العبد فكان هو بعينه معموله فانصرفت إليه الآية بخلاف قوله تعالى: أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنْحِتُونَ لأن النحت غير المنحوت، ولا اتحاد بينهما عندهم، وكان المنحوت عين الصنم، وأما فيما نحن فيه فبخلافه، والله الموفق. وبهذا يجيبهم من زعم اتحاد الفعل والمفعول ممن ساعدنا في هذه المسألة وبالله المعونة.
And some of the mutakallimūn answered that the verse, since it admits of two meanings – that is, this word is sometimes mentioned intending by it the object worked upon (al-ma'mūl), and sometimes intending by it the action (al-'amal) – is carried upon both of them. But in this there is weakness due to making the common term inclusive, and it is not sound. Then, among what invalidates the interpretation according to the principle of the Mu'tazila is that according to them the act (al-fi'l) and the object (al-maf'ūl) are one, so the action (al-'amal) and the object worked upon (al-ma'mūl) are one. And the idol (al-ṣanam) is not an action of the servant by customary usage, so it is not his object worked upon. As for the action in the idol, it is the servant's action, so it is precisely his object worked upon, so the verse turns to it. This is unlike His statement, exalted: 'Do you worship what you carve?' because carving (al-naḥt) is other than the carved object (al-manḥūt), and there is no union between them according to them, and the carved object is precisely the idol. As for what we are dealing with, it is otherwise. And God is the Grantor of success. And with this he answers them, he who claims the union of act and object, among those who agree with us in this issue. And with God is the help.
Source pages p. 870

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a Mu'tazilite interpretation of a Quranic verse, presumably one that seems to ascribe creation to idols or to other than God. The author first reports an answer given by some mutakallimūn: the word used in the verse can mean either the action or the object acted upon, so the verse is taken in both senses. But Imam Nasafi judges this answer as weak because it makes an equivocal term inclusive without justification. Then he provides a stronger refutation based on the Mu'tazilites' own principle that the act and the object are one (الفعل والمفعول واحد). According to this principle, the action and the object worked upon are identical. The idol is not an action of the servant by convention (al-'ahd), so it is not his object. However, the action performed upon the idol (e.g., carving) is the servant's act, and since act and object are one, that act is precisely the object worked upon; thus the verse's reference to 'what you worship' or similar turns to the servant's own act of carving or crafting. The author then contrasts this with the verse 'Do you worship what you carve?' (أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنْحِتُونَ), where the carving (the act) is distinct from the carved object (the idol), so no union applies. This refutation is effective because it uses the Mu'tazilites' own premises to show that their interpretation leads to an absurdity. The passage concludes that this is how one responds to those who assert the union of act and object from among those who agree with us on this issue.

Key Terms

معتزلة
فعل
مفعول
معمول

صنم
نحت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazilite principle of unity of act and object supports their interpretation of the verse about creation.
Correction: In fact, the principle undermines their interpretation because the idol is not an action, so the verb's object cannot be the idol if act and object are identical.

Checkpoint
What is the main weakness that Imam Nasafi finds in the answer given by some mutakallimūn regarding the interpretation of the verse?
A) They ignore the context of the verse.
B) They make an equivocal term inclusive without justification.
C) They reject the Mu'tazilite principle of the unity of act and object.
D) They misinterpret the meaning of the word 'idol'.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite claim that act and object are identical turns against them when applied to idol worship, because the idol is not an act of the servant.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever considered that your acts of worship might become misdirected when you focus more on the rituals themselves than on the One you are worshiping? How can this lesson's refutation of reducing worship to human actions guard your heart against such self-deception?
?
The Mu'tazilites' error began with a philosophical premise. Where in your own life have you allowed a theoretical principle to lead you away from the plain meaning of revelation? Will you commit to prioritizing scripture over human reasoning, even when it challenges your assumptions?
?
This passage shows that even good intentions (defending God's transcendence) can lead to a twisted understanding if built on wrong foundations. What beliefs are you holding onto that might be subtly undermining your submission to Allah, and are you willing to have them exposed and corrected?

Refuting the Mu'tazili Interpretation of 'Ala Ya'lamu Man Khalaq'
Nasafi refutes Mu'tazili interpretation of 67:14

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Nasafi considers the Mu'tazili interpretation of 'Ala ya'lamu man khalaq' to be a corrupt interpretation that annuls the verse's meaning of threat.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazili interpretation of 'Ala ya'lamu man khalaq' makes God's speech futile.

This passage confronts a key Mu'tazili hermeneutical move: reinterpreting the Qur'anic verse 'Does He not know who created?' (67:14) to avoid attributing knowledge of human actions to God. Nasafi demonstrates that their reading not only misses the verse's threatening tone but also renders it logically empty. Understanding his refutation clarifies proper tafsir methodology and defends divine omniscience.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazili interpretation
Begin by carefully reading the Mu'tazili claim that 'man' does not refer to God but is an object. Note their two possible readings.
This is the view Nasafi will refute.
2
Identify Nasafi's judgment
Nasafi calls this interpretation 'corrupt' and says it amounts to annulment of the verse. Notice his strong language.
He doesn't just disagree; he says it destroys the verse's meaning.
3
Analyze the threat context
Nasafi points out that the verse is a threat, like 'Do what you will; indeed He is seeing of what you do'. Understand how this context supports the apparent meaning.
The threat requires that God knows both hidden and open speech.
4
Consider the logical conclusion
Nasafi argues that the Mu'tazili reading would make the verse 'devoid of benefit' and fall under 'futility'. Reflect on why this is a serious criticism.
This shows the interpretation contradicts the purpose of revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتأويل المعتزلة أن كلمة "من" ليست براجعه إلى الله تعالى وليست هي الفاعلة بفعل يعلم بل هي مفعولة والفاعل مضمر وهو اسم الله تعالى، وتقدير الآية ألا يعلم الله من خلق ثم بعد ذلك يحتمل أن يكون قوله : خلق، فعلاً لله تعالى واقعًا على كلمة "من" فيكون تقدير الآية: ألا يعلم الله من خلقهم، ويحتمل أن يكون قوله: خلق، فعلا لمن فيكون تقدير الآية: ألا يعلم الله من خلق القول وأسره وجهر به، هذا تأويل فاسد بل هو إبطال الآية، فإن الآية وردت مورد التوعد كقوله تعالى: أَعْمَلُوا مَا شِلْتُمْ إِنَّهُ بِمَا تَعْمَلُونَ بَصِيرٌ ) أي أن الله عليم بأقوالكم أسررتم بها أو جهرتم، غير أنه خص المضمر من القول بالعلم لما أن إثبات العلم به إثبات للعلم بما جهر به منه ضرورة وإثبات العلم بذلك إثبات المجازات كما في قوله : (اعْمَلُواْ مَا سنتُمْ * وذا ظاهر في مبتذل الكلام ثم خرج قوله : أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ مخرج تقدير العلم بذلك على ما قررنا، ولذا خرج عقيب إثبات العلم به، كما يقال: إنه عالم بأخلاق فلان ومذاهبه وطرائقه وضرابته، ألا يعلم من صحبه مدة عمره وطول حياته؟ ثم ليس في إثبات العلم بمن خلق الله تعالى إثبات للعلم بما لم يخلقه وإن كان فعلاً له، كما ليس في إثبات تخليق الأنفس إثبات تخليق أفعالها عند المعتزلة، فيصير قوله: ﴿أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ خاليًا عن الفائدة خارجًا على حكم العبث – جل الله عمن يكون هذا وصف كلامه.
And the interpretation of the Mu'tazila is that the word 'man' does not refer to God Most High, and it is not the agent doing an act that is known, but rather it is the object and the subject is implied, which is the name of God Most High. The estimation of the verse is: 'Does God not know whom He created?' Then after that it is possible that His saying 'khalaqa' is an act of God Most High occurring upon the word 'man', so the estimation of the verse is: 'Does God not know whom He created?' And it is possible that His saying 'khalaqa' is an act of 'man', so the estimation of the verse is: 'Does God not know who created the saying and its secret and what is voiced aloud?' This is a corrupt interpretation; rather it is an annulment of the verse. For the verse came in the context of threat, like His saying: 'Do what you will; indeed He is seeing of what you do' (41:40), meaning God is knowledgeable of your statements, whether you keep them secret or voice them aloud. However, He specified the hidden part of speech with knowledge because establishing knowledge of it is establishing knowledge of what is voiced aloud from it by necessity, and establishing knowledge of that establishes metaphors as in His saying: 'Do what you will.' And this is apparent in vulgar speech. Then His saying: 'Does He not know who created?' came out in the mode of establishing knowledge of that according to what we have determined. That is why it came out following the establishment of knowledge of it, just as it is said: 'He knows the character of so-and-so, his doctrines, his ways, and his habits. Does He not know who accompanied him for the duration of his life and his full life?' Then there is not in establishing knowledge of whom God created an establishment of knowledge of what He did not create, even if it is His act, just as there is not in establishing the creation of souls an establishment of the creation of their actions according to the Mu'tazila. Therefore His saying 'Does He not know who created?' becomes devoid of benefit, falling under the category of futility—exalted is God above one whose speech is such.
Source pages p. 874

Commentary
This passage refutes the Mu'tazili interpretation of the Qur'anic verse 'Does He not know who created?' (67:14). The author begins by stating the Mu'tazili claim: they interpret 'man' (who) as not referring to God but as an object, with the implied subject being God. They propose two possible readings: either 'God knows whom He created' or 'God knows who created the speech.' The author declares this interpretation corrupt, amounting to an annulment of the verse. He argues that the verse is a threat, similar to 'Do what you will; indeed He is seeing of what you do' (41:40), where God's knowledge encompasses inner and outer speech. The specification of hidden speech does not exclude outward speech. The author explains that the verse's construction implies that knowledge of created beings necessarily includes knowledge of their actions, but this does not mean God knows things He did not create. He concludes that the Mu'tazili interpretation renders the verse meaningless and futile, which is beneath God's speech.

المعتزلة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazili interpretation of 'Ala ya'lamu man khalaq' is a plausible grammatical alternative that does not change the meaning.
Correction: Nasafi shows that this interpretation actually annuls the verse's intended meaning of threat and makes it a statement of futility.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is the main consequence of the Mu'tazili interpretation of the verse 'Ala ya'lamu man khalaq'?
A) It clarifies God's knowledge.
B) It annuls the verse and makes it meaningless.
C) It proves that humans create their own actions.
D) It confirms the apparent meaning.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazili interpretation of 'Ala ya'lamu man khalaq' is not just a different reading; it annuls the verse's purpose and renders it a statement of futility.

?
The Mu'tazili interpretation made the verse futile by removing its threat. Is there a verse in the Quran that you have ignored or explained away because its warning made you uncomfortable? What would it cost you to take that verse literally today?
?
God knows every secret thought and word you have ever uttered. Does that comfort you or terrify you? How would your life change if you truly believed that nothing you think or say is hidden from Him?

Nasafi's Fourfold Refutation of al-Ka'bi's Division of Agency
Nasafi refutes al-Ka'bi's division of action and attribute with four arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's four arguments refuting al-Ka'bi's claim that the human causes the action and God causes its quality, and why dividing agency leads to theological absurdities.

Core Idea
Dividing agency between human and God leads to shirk and attributing folly to God.

Nasafi now tackles a specific objection from the Mu'tazilite al-Ka'bi, who attempted to resolve the problem of evil by splitting causation: the human causes the action (e.g., disbelief) while God causes its quality (e.g., evil). This passage presents al-Ka'bi's reasoning and Nasafi's sharp four-point rebuttal. By studying these refutations, you will see how Maturidi theology firmly rejects any form of partnership in divine actions.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Ka'bi's objection
Begin by reading the opening section where al-Ka'bi's view is presented: the servant originates the action while God originates its attribute (the evil). Notice the examples (walking, harming, paining).
This objection attempts to preserve both human responsibility and divine omnipotence.
2
Identify the four refutations
Nasafi gives four numbered points. List each one: (1) leads to jihāt al-fi'l, (2) admits maqdūr al-fi'l, (3) establishes shirk, (4) implies God originates evil, which they consider safah.
Each refutation is based on the Mu'tazilites' own principles.
3
Understand the logical force of each refutation
For each point, grasp why it is a reductio ad absurdum. For example, the fourth point: if God creates the evil attribute, He creates evil itself, and the Mu'tazilites say the originator of evil is foolish, so God would be foolish—impossible.
Nasafi uses the opponents' own definitions against them.
4
Reflect on the broader significance
Consider why this refutation is important for Maturidi theology: it upholds tawḥīd in actions and rejects any dualistic causation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: لما كانت صفات الأفعال راجعة إلى أعيانها فالكفر إذا فعل وهو قبيح فيتولى العبد إيجاده من حيث الكفر، ويتولى الله تعالى إيجاده من حيث القبح، وكذا هذا في المشي والإيذاء والإيلام، وهذا معنى ما ذكر الكعبي أن العبد مختار من فعله مضطر في تألمه، والمختار عنده من تولى إيجاد الكفر، والمضطر عنده من تولى غيره إيجاد صفة فيه لا قدرة له عليها. قيل: هذا السؤال على أصلكم فاسد من وجوه: أحدها: أنه يوجب القول بجهات الفعل وهو عندكم باطل. والآخر: اعتراف بما جعلتموه من أقوى الشبهات لكم في المسألة وهو دخول مقدور الفعل والقول بذلك باطل. والثالث: أن هذا عندكم إثبات الشرك بين الله تعالى وبين العبد في هذا الفعل، والقول بذلك باطل. والرابع: أن موجد القبح الراجع إلى ذات القبيح كان موجدًا للقبيح، وعندكم موجد القبح سفيه والله تعالى يتعالى عن فعل السفه بلا خلاف بيننا وبينكم وإن كان عندكم موصوفا بالقدرة عليه.
If they say: Since the attributes of actions refer back to their essences, disbelief when done is evil; then the servant undertakes its origination in terms of disbelief, and God undertakes its origination in terms of evil. Likewise in walking, harming, and paining. This is the meaning of what al-Ka'bī mentioned: the servant is free in his action, constrained in his suffering. According to him, the free agent is the one who undertakes the origination of disbelief, and the constrained is one for whom another undertakes the origination of an attribute in him over which he has no power. It is said: This question according to your own principle is invalid in several ways: First, it necessitates the doctrine of aspects of the action, which according to you is false. Second, it is an admission of what you consider one of the strongest doubts for you in the issue, namely the entry of the capability of the action, and that doctrine is false. Third, this according to you is establishing partnership between God and the servant in this action, and that doctrine is false. Fourth, the originator of evil that refers back to the essence of the evil thing is the originator of the evil, and according to you, the originator of evil is foolish, and God is exalted above acting foolishly without dispute between us and you, even if according to you He is described as having power over it.
Source pages p. 880

Commentary
This passage presents a second objection attributed to al-Ka'bī and a fourfold refutation. The objectors, following al-Ka'bī, argue that because attributes of actions are identical to their essences, the servant causes the action qua disbelief, and God causes it qua evil. This would make the servant free regarding the action but constrained regarding its quality. Nasafi responds with four refutations: (1) This implies the doctrine of aspects (jihāt) of the action, i.e., that the same action has different aspects from different agents, which is condemned by both Sunnis and Mu'tazilites. (2) It admits that the capability (maqdūr) of the action enters into the debate, which the Mu'tazilites consider a strong argument against them, but this admission is false. (3) It establishes shirk between God and the servant in the same action, which is invalid. (4) Whoever originates the evil attribute also originates the evil essence; thus God would be the originator of evil, and according to the Mu'tazilites, the originator of evil is foolish (safīh), but God is exonerated from foolishness. This is a reductio ad absurdum: the view leads to attributing folly to God, which is impossible.

Key Terms
الكعبي
جهات الفعل
شرك
سفه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that dividing agency between human (action) and God (quality) is a reasonable compromise to solve the problem of evil.
Correction: Nasafi shows that this division leads to shirk (partnership with God) and the absurd conclusion that God is foolish, since He would be the originator of evil.

Checkpoint
What is one of Nasafi's refutations of al-Ka'bī's view?
A) It leads to belief in fatalism
B) It implies God is the originator of evil, which the Mu'tazilites consider foolish
C) It denies human freedom
D) It contradicts the Quran

Key Takeaway
Nasafi refutes al-Ka'bī's division of agency by showing that it contradicts Mu'tazilite principles and leads to shirk and attributing folly to God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, do you ever catch yourself attributing your good deeds to your own effort and your bad deeds to circumstances or even to God? How does Nasafi’s argument that dividing agency leads to shirk challenge you to acknowledge God’s sole sovereignty over all actions, including your own? What concrete step can you take today to repent from that subtle shirk?
?
Nasafi’s fourth argument shows that if God were the originator of the evil attribute, He would be called foolish—a conclusion the Mu'tazilites reject. But you and I often complain about God's decree when something bad happens. Do you realize that complaining implies you believe God should not have created that evil? How does this lesson expose the need to trust God’s wisdom even when you cannot see it? Will you commit to praising Him for everything, even the trials?
?
The Mu'tazilites tried to protect God’s justice by dividing agency. But Nasafi proves this compromise actually diminishes God. Are there areas in your faith where you try to 'protect' God’s honor by limiting His control, such as in your prayers or your theology? What would it look like for you to fully submit to God’s absolute power and wisdom without reservation, starting today?

The Mu'tazilite Self-Destruction: Tawhid and 'Adl
The author critiques the Mu'tazilite position for undermining tawhid by their concept of 'adl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Mu'tazilite attempts to uphold divine justice ('adl) and unity (tawhid) logically undermine each other, leading to internal contradictions.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila's 'adl destroys their tawhid, and their tawhid destroys their 'adl.

This passage presents a powerful critique of the Mu'tazilites from within their own framework. The author demonstrates that their concept of 'adl forces them to compromise tawhid, and their concept of tawhid forces them to compromise 'adl. Moreover, their own doctrines of ability (istitā'a) and divine attributes lead to further contradictions. This lesson unpacks the key arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note the author's argumentative flow.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the first critique: creative power incapacitates God
Find where the author argues that affirming creative power for servants implies God can be incapacitated, which would allow polytheism.
This links to the earlier discussion on divine unity.
3
Understand the second critique: attributes annul command
Trace the argument that denying God's attributes (like speech) to uphold tawhid leads to annulling His command and prohibition, making acts meaningless and punishment unjust.
4
Grasp the symmetrical dictum
Note the famous phrase: 'They annulled their 'adl by their tawhid and their tawhid by their 'adl.' Also consider the alternative formulation.
The author adds that they even annul each by themselves.
5
Analyze the third critique: istitā'a before action fails
Understand the argument that affirming ability before the act but denying it at the time of action makes the obligation impossible, thus unjust.
This shows their 'adl nullifies itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما قلنا: إنه يؤدي إلى إبطال دلائل الموحدين، لأنه يؤدي إلى تعجيز الباري على ما بينا، ولو جاز أن يكون الباري جل وعلا عاجزا بتعجيز الغير إياه ولا تبطل ربوبيته لجاز أن يكون للعالم صانعان وأكثر ، وإن كان البعض يعجز بعضا، وقد قررنا هذا الفصل على الاستقصاء (۱) في (۲) مسألة إثبات وحدانية القديم جل جلاله فلا نعيدها هاهنا. ثم المعتزلة إنما يثبتون لغير الله تعالى قدرة التخليق لئلا يكون الله تعالى معاقبًا عباده على ما يخلق هو بنفسه ويخرجه من العدم إلى الوجود، فيكون عادلاً في تعذيبهم غير ظالم في عقابهم، فأبطلوا التوحيد بهذا العدل، وقد بينا أنهم حيث أنكروا أن يكون الكلام معنى قائمًا بذات الله تعالى أو شيء من الصفات بل قالوا بذات لا صفة له تحقيقا للتوحيد فأبطلوا أمره ونهيه وبطل بذلك الحل والحرمة وخرج الفعل عن كونه طاعة أو معصية، وكان التعذيب على ما ليس بمعصية ظلمًا فأبطلوا عدلهم بتوحيدهم، وهذا معنى قول أصحابنا إن المعتزلة أبطلوا عدلهم بتوحيدهم) (٤) وتوحيدهم بعدلهم ) () ( ولو قيل : إنهم أبطلوا عدلهم بعدلهم وتوحيدهم بتوحيدهم) (٦) لكان صوابًا ، وبيانه أنهم أثبتوا الاستطاعة سابقة على الفعل لئلا يؤدي إلى تكليف ما لا يطاق، ثم قررنا أنها تنعدم عند الفعل فإذا كان فعل عندهم لا قدرة للفاعل عليه، وما لا قدرة للفاعل عليه كان تكليفه تكليف ما لا يطاق، والأمر به والنهي عنه باطل والتعذيب عليه ظلم فأبطلوا عدلهم بعدلهم، وأبطلوا توحيدهم بتوحيدهم، فإنه لو جاز وجود العالم بذات لا حياة له ولا قدرة ولا علم ولا سمع ولا
And we only said: It leads to invalidating the proofs of the monotheists, because it leads to incapacitating the Creator as we clarified. And if it were permissible that the Creator, glorious and exalted, be incapacitated by the incapacitation of another without His lordship being invalidated, it would be permissible that the world have two or more makers, even if some incapacitate others. And we have settled this section in detail (1) in (2) the issue of establishing the oneness of the Eternal, glorious be His majesty, so we do not repeat it here. Then the Mu'tazila only affirm creative power for other than Allah the Exalted so that Allah the Exalted not be punishing His servants for what He Himself creates and brings from non-existence to existence, thus being just in their torment and not unjust in their punishment. So they annulled tawhid by this 'adl. And we have shown that when they denied that speech is a meaning subsisting in the essence of Allah or anything of the attributes, rather they said [He has] an essence without attributes to realize tawhid, they annulled His command and prohibition, and with that the lawful and the prohibited became void, and the act ceased to be obedience or disobedience, and torment for what is not disobedience became injustice. So they annulled their 'adl by their tawhid. This is the meaning of our companions’ statement: The Mu'tazila annulled their 'adl by their tawhid (4) and their tawhid by their 'adl. And if it were said: They annulled their 'adl by their 'adl and their tawhid by their tawhid (6), it would be correct. Its explanation: They affirmed ability (istitā'a) prior to the action to avoid leading to obligation of what is beyond capacity. Then we established that it ceases at the action. So when an action occurs, according to them, there is no power for the agent over it. And what the agent has no power over, its obligation is an obligation of what is beyond capacity. Command and prohibition regarding it are invalid, and torment upon it is injustice. So they annulled their 'adl by their 'adl, and they annulled their tawhid by their tawhid. For if it were permissible for the world to exist from an essence that has no life, no power, no knowledge, no hearing, and no...
Source pages p. 888

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite position. The author begins by restating the conclusion from the previous argument: affirming creative power for the servant leads to invalidating the proofs of the monotheists, because it implies incapacitating God. If incapacitation of God were possible, polytheism would be possible. Then the author directly attacks the Mu'tazilite motivation: they affirm creative power for others to avoid God punishing for His own creation, thus maintaining His justice ('adl). However, in doing so they annul tawhid. Then the author shows a deeper contradiction: The Mu'tazila, in their effort to uphold tawhid, deny that God has attributes such as speech subsisting in His essence, saying He is an essence without attributes. This annuls His command and prohibition, making lawful and unlawful meaningless, and acts become neither obedience nor disobedience. Consequently, torment for any act becomes unjust, annulling their 'adl by their tawhid. The author then explains the famous dictum: 'The Mu'tazila annulled their 'adl by their tawhid and their tawhid by their 'adl.' He even suggests that a more accurate statement would be that they annul each by themselves. The explanation: they affirm ability (istitā'a) before the act to avoid impossible obligation, but they also hold that ability ceases at the act. Thus at the time of action, the agent has no power, so the act is obligated beyond capacity, making the obligation unjust. Thus their 'adl (based on ability before the act) is annulled by their own 'adl (since the act becomes impossible), and their tawhid (denying attributes) is annulled by their tawhid (since the world would exist from an essence without attributes). The passage cuts off while continuing the critique.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila successfully harmonize tawhid and 'adl in a coherent system.
Correction: The author demonstrates that their attempts to uphold each concept actually undermine the other, leading to self-contradiction. Their 'adl destroys tawhid, and their tawhid destroys 'adl.

Checkpoint
According to the author, how do the Mu'tazila annul their 'adl by their 'adl?
A) By affirming that God is just in punishing servants for His own acts.
B) By affirming ability before the act but holding it ceases at the act, making the obligation impossible.
C) By denying God's attributes, which makes command and prohibition void.
D) By affirming creative power for the servant, which leads to polytheism.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite concepts of 'adl and tawhid are internally self-defeating and cannot be consistently maintained together.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you try to defend God's justice by reworking His attributes, as the Mu'tazila did, have you ever stopped to consider that you might be emptying His commands of all meaning? If acts are no longer obedience or disobedience, what is left of your relationship with Him? Will you repent of any way you have done this in your heart?
?
The Mu'tazila annulled their 'adl by their own 'adl— they constructed a 'justice' that made accountability impossible. Where in your life have you set up a standard of fairness that actually excuses you from obeying a clear command of Allah? What would it cost you to abandon that standard and submit entirely?
?
If the Mu'tazila's pursuit of tawhid led them to deny God's attributes, what cherished belief of yours about God might be subtly leading you to a lesser understanding of His majesty? Are you willing to let His revealed attributes remain mysterious and real, even if they challenge your logic? When will you surrender your mind to the Qur'an and Sunnah instead of your own reasoning?
