Mu'ammar's View and Its First Two Corruptions
Al-Nasafi states Mu'ammar's view and identifies two corruptions: making lifeless agents creators of precise actions, and giving God partners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Mu'ammar's claim that bodies create accidents and why al-Nasafi considers this to make lifeless agents creators and give God partners.

Core Idea
Mu'ammar's view turns inanimate bodies into creators of precise actions, undermining divine uniqueness.

Al-Nasafi begins by restating Mu'ammar's position that God only creates substances, while bodies produce accidents. He then identifies the first two major corruptions: that this allows sound, precise actions to come from lifeless things, and that it makes God have partners in creation. These points strike at the heart of Islamic monotheism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand Mu'ammar's original claim.
2
Identify the two corruptions
Notice how al-Nasafi enumerates the first two problems: (1) accidents as precise actions from lifeless agents, (2) partnership in creation.
3
Reflect on the implications
Ask yourself: why is it problematic for a lifeless object to produce a precise action? How does this relate to the proof of God's attributes?
Consider the principle that a precise action indicates a knowledgeable, powerful agent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بصر لجاز وجود كل جزء من أجزاء العالم بكل جماد وموات، ولم يبق دليل على وجوده بالله تعالى، وصار كل موات وجماد جائز الألوهية ممكن الربوبية. قول معمر يؤدي إلى المحالات: وإنما قلنا: إنه يؤدي إلى القول بصانعين، وذلك لأن العالم أعراض وأعيان والله تعالى خالق الأعيان، فأما الأعراض فعلى قول معمر رئيس المعتزلة: لا قدرة الله تعالى على شيء من الأعراض وما تولى هو خلقها ولا إيجادها ولا داخلة تحت قدرته، إنما الأجسام هي التي تخلق الأعراض بعضها بطباعها وبعضها بالاختيار، فما خلق الله تعالى عنده لا صحة ولا سقما ولا موتا ولا حياة ولا لونا ولا رائحة ولا طعماً ولا هيئة ولا تركيبا ولا تأليفًا ولا حركة ولا سكونًا، وغير ذلك وفيه فساد من وجوه: أحدها: أنه جوز تخليق الأعراض من الموات والجمادات ولا حياة لها ولا قدرة ولا علم، وتلك الأعراض أفعال محكمة متقنة وتجويز تخليقها ممن لا علم له ولا قدرة ولا حياة يبطل كون الصانع موصوفا بهذه الصفات، إذ الفعل المحكم المتقن دليل ثبوت هذه الصفات، ولا بداهة للعقول تحكم عليه بالجهل والحمق حيث جوز الأفعال المحكمة ممن لا حياة له ولا علم ولا قدرة. والآخر أنه جعل الله تعالى شركاء في تخليق العالم إذ العالم لما كان منقسما ولم يكن منه إلا قسم واحد ، وكان القسم الآخر حاصلاً بغيره كان العالم مخلوقا له ولغيره، ثم كان قوله شرًا من قول المجوس بوجوه: أحدها: أن المجوس لا تثبت للصانع إلا شريكاً واحدًا، وهو أثبت ما لا يحصى من الشركاء. والثاني: أنه جوز وجود الفعل المحكم المتقن ممن لا حياة له ولا علم ولا قدرة. والمجوس أنكروا ذلك. وهو أثبت الله تعالى شركاء غير أحياء لا علماء لا قادرين والمجوس لم يجوزوا ذلك. والثالث: أنه جعل صنع كل جماد وموات وأكثر من صنع الله تعالى، لأن الله تعالى لم يخلق إلا الأجسام ثم كل جسم خلقه يخلق إما باختياره وإما بالطبع ما لا يحصى من الأعراض، فيكون بمقابلته كل فرد من أجسام العالم الذي تولى الله تعالى تخليقه ما لا يحصى كثرة مما لا يخلقه الله تعالى. والرابع: أن المجوس ما أضافوا إلى غير الصانع الحكيم إلا الشرور والقبائح تنزيها له، وهو كما أضاف الشرور والقبائح من الموت والسقم والمرض والزمانة والعمى والصم والعرج والشلل إلى غير الله تعالى أضاف أيضا المحاسن والخيرات من الفرح والسرور واللذة والحياة والصحة والبصر والسمع إلى غير الله تعالى، فضاهى المجوس في إضافة الشرور إلى غير الله تعالى، وأربى عليهم بإضافة الخيرات والمحاسن إلى غير الله. ثم العلم بحدوث الأجسام يحصل بمعرفة حدوث الأعراض، والأعراض ليست بمخلوقة الله فلم يكن الله تعالى مثبتاً دلالة حدوث العالم ولا قادرًا على إثباته. وإنما أثبت ذلك غيره وهو الأجسام، وكذلك ما أثبت الرسول دلالة الصدق إذ ما
It became permissible for every part of the world to exist from every inanimate and dead thing, and no proof remained for His existence by Allah Almighty, and every dead and inanimate thing became a possible object of divinity and a possible lordship. The statement of Mu'ammar leads to impossibilities: And we only said: it leads to the assertion of two creators, because the world consists of accidents (a'rad) and substances (a'yan), and Allah Almighty is the Creator of substances. As for accidents, according to the statement of Mu'ammar, the chief of the Mu'tazila: Allah Almighty has no power over any accident, and He did not undertake their creation nor their bringing into existence, and they are not under His power; rather, bodies are what create accidents, some by their natures and some by choice. So according to him, Allah did not create health, nor sickness, nor death, nor life, nor color, nor smell, nor taste, nor shape, nor composition, nor arrangement, nor movement, nor stillness, nor other than that. And in it there is corruption in several respects: One of them: that he permitted the creation of accidents from inanimate and dead things, while they have no life, no power, and no knowledge. And those accidents are sound, precise actions. Permitting their creation from one who has no knowledge, no power, and no life invalidates the Creator being described with these attributes, for a sound, precise action is a proof of the affirmation of these attributes. And there is no innate intuition of the intellects that would rule that ignorance and foolishness where he permitted sound actions from one who has no life, knowledge, or power. Another: that he made Allah Almighty have partners in the creation of the world, because when the world is divided, and only one part comes from Him, and the other part comes from something else, then the world is created by Him and by other than Him. Then his statement was worse than the statement of the Magians in several ways: One of them: that the Magians only affirm one partner for the Creator, while he affirmed countless partners. The second: that he permitted the existence of a sound, precise action from one who has no life, knowledge, or power. The Magians denied that. And he affirmed for Allah partners that are not living, not knowing, not powerful, while the Magians did not permit that. The third: that he made the making of every inanimate and dead thing greater than the making of Allah Almighty, because Allah did not create except bodies, then every body He creates creates, either by choice or by nature, countless accidents. So in contrast, every individual body of the world whose creation Allah undertook has countless things that Allah does not create. The fourth: that the Magians only attributed to other than the wise Creator evil things (shurur) and ugly things (qaba'ih) to exalt Him, while he, just as he attributed evil and ugly things like death, sickness, disease, chronic illness, blindness, deafness, lameness, and paralysis to other than Allah, also attributed good things (mahasn) and blessings (khayrat) like joy, happiness, pleasure, life, health, sight, and hearing to other than Allah. So he emulated the Magians in attributing evil to other than Allah, and surpassed them in attributing good and beautiful things to other than Allah. Then knowledge of the temporality of bodies is obtained by knowing the temporality of accidents, and accidents are not created by Allah, so Allah did not establish the proof of the temporality of the world, nor is He capable of proving it. Rather, someone else, namely bodies, established that. Likewise, the Messenger did not establish the proof of truthfulness since...
Source pages p. 889

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Mu'ammar's theological position regarding the creation of accidents. Al-Nasafi begins by summarizing Mu'ammar's view: that the world consists of substances (a'yan) and accidents (a'rad), and God only creates the substances, while bodies themselves create accidents—some by their innate nature (tab') and some by choice (ikhtiyar). Consequently, God does not create any accidents like health, sickness, color, movement, etc. Al-Nasafi then attacks this view, stating that it leads to several corruptions. The first corruption is that it permits accidents—which are precise, well-ordered actions—to be produced by inanimate, lifeless things that lack knowledge, power, and life. This contradicts the evidentiary role of actions: a sound, precise action points to the agent having knowledge and power. Allowing such actions from a lifeless source would mean the Creator might not have these attributes, which is absurd. The second corruption is that it makes God have partners in creation, because the world is divided: one part (substances) comes from God, the other part (accidents) comes from bodies. This effectively makes the world created by God and others, resulting in many partners. Al-Nasafi then argues that Mu'ammar's view is even worse than the dualism of the Magians (Zoroastrians) in four respects. First, the Magians only posit one partner (the principle of evil), while Mu'ammar posits countless partners (each body that creates accidents). Second, the Magians deny that precise actions can come from lifeless agents, but Mu'ammar affirms this. Third, Mu'ammar's view attributes more acts of creation to bodies than to God, since bodies create countless accidents while God only creates bodies. Fourth, the Magians only attribute evil to the other principle to preserve God's goodness, but Mu'ammar attributes both evil and good to other than God, thus surpassing the Magians in associating partners. Finally, Al-Nasafi points out a devastating consequence: the proof of the world's temporality depends on the temporality of accidents. If accidents are not created by God, then God cannot prove the world's temporality; rather, bodies would be the ones establishing that proof. Similarly, the proof of the Prophet's truthfulness (through miracles, which are accidents) would also be attributed to other than God, undermining revelation.

Mu'ammar
أعراض
أعيان
تخليق
فعل محكم متقن

What is the first corruption al-Nasafi identifies in Mu'ammar's view?
A) It denies the existence of God
B) It allows lifeless things to create precise actions
C) It makes God a Magian
D) It denies accidents exist

Key Takeaway
Mu'ammar's view that bodies create accidents leads to the absurdities of lifeless agents producing precise actions and God having partners in creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that God creates every detail of your life—including your health, your skills, even your complex thoughts—how would that change the way you pray when facing a challenge? Would you still turn to other means as ultimate causes, or rely solely on Him? Consider one area where you've acted as if 'accidents' happen without His involvement. What specific step can you take today to affirm His sole power in that area?
?
The passage says that permitting sound actions from lifeless things invalidates the proof that the Creator has knowledge and power. Where in your own heart have you attributed precise, good outcomes to mere chance, your own intelligence, or other secondary causes? How does that subtle attribution steal glory from God? What will you do to consciously return that credit to Him this week?
?
Mu'ammar's view effectively gave partners to God in creation. Do you ever give partners to God in your trust—believing that some aspect of your security depends more on a person, a job, or a plan than on God's direct control? How would your daily worry change if you internalized that every accident and substance comes only from Him? What is one decision you can make today that demonstrates that conviction?

Worse Than the Magians: Four Ways Mu'ammar's View Exceeds Dualism
Al-Nasafi shows Mu'ammar's view is worse than Magian dualism in four ways and concludes it undermines proofs of God and prophecy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will see how al-Nasafi demonstrates that Mu'ammar's position is even more problematic than Magian dualism on four counts and that it undermines the proofs for God and prophecy.

Core Idea
Mu'ammar's view is worse than outright dualism because it multiplies partners and attributes both good and evil to them.

After exposing the first two corruptions, al-Nasafi compares Mu'ammar's view to the Magians (Zoroastrians), who believe in a second evil creator. He lists four ways Mu'ammar surpasses them in error. Then he points out a devastating consequence: if accidents are not created by God, then the proof of the world's temporality and the proof of the Prophet's truthfulness are both attributed to other than God.

Guided Path
1
Read the comparison with Magians
Carefully read the four points where Mu'ammar's view is worse than the Magians.
2
Understand the final consequence
Notice how al-Nasafi ties the argument to epistemology: without God creating accidents, the proofs of temporality and prophecy fail.
3
Reflect on the gravity
Consider why al-Nasafi considers this a massive theological error.
This consequence undermines the very foundations of tawhid and risalah.

بصر لجاز وجود كل جزء من أجزاء العالم بكل جماد وموات، ولم يبق دليل على وجوده بالله تعالى، وصار كل موات وجماد جائز الألوهية ممكن الربوبية. قول معمر يؤدي إلى المحالات: وإنما قلنا: إنه يؤدي إلى القول بصانعين، وذلك لأن العالم أعراض وأعيان والله تعالى خالق الأعيان، فأما الأعراض فعلى قول معمر رئيس المعتزلة: لا قدرة الله تعالى على شيء من الأعراض وما تولى هو خلقها ولا إيجادها ولا داخلة تحت قدرته، إنما وغير ذلك وفيه فساد من وجوه: أحدها: أنه جوز تخليق الأعراض من الموات والجمادات ولا حياة لها ولا قدرة ولا علم، وتلك الأعراض أفعال محكمة متقنة وتجويز تخليقها ممن لا علم له ولا قدرة ولا حياة يبطل كون الصانع موصوفا بهذه الصفات، إذ الفعل المحكم المتقن دليل ثبوت هذه الصفات، ولا بداهة للعقول تحكم عليه بالجهل والحمق حيث جوز الأفعال المحكمة ممن لا حياة له ولا علم ولا قدرة. والآخر أنه جعل الله تعالى شركاء في تخليق العالم إذ العالم لما كان منقسما ولم يكن منه إلا قسم واحد ، وكان القسم الآخر حاصلاً بغيره كان العالم مخلوقا له ولغيره، ثم كان قوله شرًا من قول المجوس بوجوه: أحدها: أن المجوس لا تثبت للصانع إلا شريكاً واحدًا، وهو أثبت ما لا يحصى من الشركاء. والثاني: أنه جوز وجود الفعل المحكم المتقن ممن لا حياة له ولا علم ولا قدرة. والمجوس أنكروا ذلك. وهو أثبت الله تعالى شركاء غير أحياء لا علماء لا قادرين والمجوس لم يجوزوا ذلك. والثالث: أنه جعل صنع كل جماد وموات وأكثر من صنع الله تعالى، لأن الله تعالى لم يخلق إلا الأجسام ثم كل جسم خلقه يخلق إما باختياره وإما بالطبع ما لا يحصى من الأعراض، فيكون بمقابلته كل فرد من أجسام العالم الذي تولى الله تعالى تخليقه ما لا يحصى كثرة مما لا يخلقه الله تعالى. والرابع: أن المجوس ما أضافوا إلى غير الصانع الحكيم إلا الشرور والقبائح تنزيها له، وهو كما أضاف الشرور والقبائح من الموت والسقم والمرض والزمانة والعمى والصم والعرج والشلل إلى غير الله تعالى أضاف أيضا المحاسن والخيرات من الفرح والسرور واللذة والحياة والصحة والبصر والسمع إلى غير الله تعالى، فضاهى المجوس في إضافة الشرور إلى غير الله تعالى، وأربى عليهم بإضافة الخيرات والمحاسن إلى غير الله. ثم العلم بحدوث الأجسام يحصل بمعرفة حدوث الأعراض، والأعراض ليست بمخلوقة الله فلم يكن الله تعالى مثبتاً دلالة حدوث العالم ولا قادرًا على إثباته. وإنما أثبت ذلك غيره وهو الأجسام، وكذلك ما أثبت الرسول دلالة الصدق إذ ما
It became permissible for every part of the world to exist from every inanimate and dead thing, and no proof remained for His existence by Allah Almighty, and every dead and inanimate thing became a possible object of divinity and a possible lordship. The statement of Mu'ammar leads to impossibilities: And we only said: it leads to the assertion of two creators, because the world consists of accidents (a'rad) and substances (a'yan), and Allah Almighty is the Creator of substances. As for accidents, according to the statement of Mu'ammar, the chief of the Mu'tazila: Allah Almighty has no power over any accident, and He did not undertake their creation nor their bringing into existence, and they are not under His power; rather, bodies are what create accidents, some by their natures and some by choice. So according to him, Allah did not create health, nor sickness, nor death, nor life, nor color, nor smell, nor taste, nor shape, nor composition, nor arrangement, nor movement, nor stillness, nor other than that. And in it there is corruption in several respects: One of them: that he permitted the creation of accidents from inanimate and dead things, while they have no life, no power, and no knowledge. And those accidents are sound, precise actions. Permitting their creation from one who has no knowledge, no power, and no life invalidates the Creator being described with these attributes, for a sound, precise action is a proof of the affirmation of these attributes. And there is no innate intuition of the intellects that would rule that ignorance and foolishness where he permitted sound actions from one who has no life, knowledge, or power. Another: that he made Allah Almighty have partners in the creation of the world, because when the world is divided, and only one part comes from Him, and the other part comes from something else, then the world is created by Him and by other than Him. Then his statement was worse than the statement of the Magians in several ways: One of them: that the Magians only affirm one partner for the Creator, while he affirmed countless partners. The second: that he permitted the existence of a sound, precise action from one who has no life, knowledge, or power. The Magians denied that. And he affirmed for Allah partners that are not living, not knowing, not powerful, while the Magians did not permit that. The third: that he made the making of every inanimate and dead thing greater than the making of Allah Almighty, because Allah did not create except bodies, then every body He creates creates, either by choice or by nature, countless accidents. So in contrast, every individual body of the world whose creation Allah undertook has countless things that Allah does not create. The fourth: that the Magians only attributed to other than the wise Creator evil things (shurur) and ugly things (qaba'ih) to exalt Him, while he, just as he attributed evil and ugly things like death, sickness, disease, chronic illness, blindness, deafness, lameness, and paralysis to other than Allah, also attributed good things (mahasn) and blessings (khayrat) like joy, happiness, pleasure, life, health, sight, and hearing to other than Allah. So he emulated the Magians in attributing evil to other than Allah, and surpassed them in attributing good and beautiful things to other than Allah. Then knowledge of the temporality of bodies is obtained by knowing the temporality of accidents, and accidents are not created by Allah, so Allah did not establish the proof of the temporality of the world, nor is He capable of proving it. Rather, someone else, namely bodies, established that. Likewise, the Messenger did not establish the proof of truthfulness since...
Source pages p. 889

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Mu'ammar's theological position regarding the creation of accidents. Al-Nasafi begins by summarizing Mu'ammar's view: that the world consists of substances (a'yan) and accidents (a'rad), and God only creates the substances, while bodies themselves create accidents—some by their innate nature (tab') and some by choice (ikhtiyar). Consequently, God does not create any accidents like health, sickness, color, movement, etc. Al-Nasafi then attacks this view, stating that it leads to several corruptions. The first corruption is that it permits accidents—which are precise, well-ordered actions—to be produced by inanimate, lifeless things that lack knowledge, power, and life. This contradicts the evidentiary role of actions: a sound, precise action points to the agent having knowledge and power. Allowing such actions from a lifeless source would mean the Creator might not have these attributes, which is absurd. The second corruption is that it makes God have partners in creation, because the world is divided: one part (substances) comes from God, the other part (accidents) comes from bodies. This effectively makes the world created by God and others, resulting in many partners. Al-Nasafi then argues that Mu'ammar's view is even worse than the dualism of the Magians (Zoroastrians) in four respects. First, the Magians only posit one partner (the principle of evil), while Mu'ammar posits countless partners (each body that creates accidents). Second, the Magians deny that precise actions can come from lifeless agents, but Mu'ammar affirms this. Third, Mu'ammar's view attributes more acts of creation to bodies than to God, since bodies create countless accidents while God only creates bodies. Fourth, the Magians only attribute evil to the other principle to preserve God's goodness, but Mu'ammar attributes both evil and good to other than God, thus surpassing the Magians in associating partners. Finally, Al-Nasafi points out a devastating consequence: the proof of the world's temporality depends on the temporality of accidents. If accidents are not created by God, then God cannot prove the world's temporality; rather, bodies would be the ones establishing that proof. Similarly, the proof of the Prophet's truthfulness (through miracles, which are accidents) would also be attributed to other than God, undermining revelation.

Key Terms
مجوس
شركاء
اختيار
طبع
بداهة

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi, in what way is Mu'ammar's view worse than the Magians regarding the attribution of good and evil?
A) He attributes only good to others
B) He attributes both good and evil to others
C) He attributes only evil to others
D) He attributes neither

Key Takeaway
Mu'ammar's claim that bodies create accidents is worse than Magian dualism and destroys the foundations for proving God's existence and prophecy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience a blessing like health, joy, or success, do you ever find yourself attributing it to your own effort, a doctor's skill, or luck—forgetting that Allah alone is the ultimate source? How does Mu'ammar's error of ascribing both good and evil to partners expose a subtle form of shirk in your own heart? What concrete step can you take today to redirect all gratitude to Allah alone?
?
In moments of hardship—such as illness, loss, or disappointment—do you instinctively blame circumstances, other people, or even yourself, as if the evil came from them independent of Allah's decree? How does this passage call you to a deeper tawheed that sees all events as from Allah while affirming that evil is not attributed to Him? Will you commit to saying 'Alhamdulillah' in the next difficulty before you complain?
?
Al-Nasafi warns that if accidents are not created by God, the very proof of His existence collapses. Do you live with the awareness that your belief in God hinges on His exclusive control over every single event—even the flicker of your consciousness? How does this truth change the way you view the seemingly 'small' occurrences in your life? Will you start your day tomorrow by consciously recognizing Allah's direct creation of every moment?

intermediate
12 min
Four Ways Dualists Surpass Magians in Error
Author enumerates four ways dualists outdo Magians in associating partners with Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four specific ways in which the dualists (Ithnayn) commit greater shirk than the Magians, as argued by Imam al-Nasafi.

Core Idea
Dualists outdo Magians by attributing both good and evil to partners, not just evil.

Imam al-Nasafi contrasts two deviant groups: the Magians who acknowledge one partner (Ahriman) for the Creator, and the dualists who proliferate partners. To highlight the gravity of dualist error, he enumerates four points where they exceed the Magians in associating partners with Allah. This lesson unpacks each point.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing. Then read the translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the author uses 'أحدها', 'والثاني', etc., marking clear enumeration.
2
Understand the comparison framework
Recognize that the Magians serve as a benchmark: they already commit shirk by affirming one partner. The dualists are worse in four specific respects.
The author is not defending Magians but using them to magnify the dualists' error.
3
Examine each of the four points
Work through each point one by one. For each, identify what the Magians affirm or deny, and how the dualists exceed them.
The four points are: (1) number of partners, (2) attribution of action to lifeless beings, (3) scope of creation, (4) attribution of goods as well as evils.
4
Reflect on the severity of dualist shirk
Consider why attributing good things to partners is worse than attributing only evils. This underscores the dualists' departure from tawhid.
The fourth point is particularly damning because it implicates Allah's goodness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحدها: أن المجوس لا تثبت للصانع إلا شريكاً واحداً، وهو أثبت ما لا يحصى من الشركاء. والثاني: أنه جوز وجود الفعل المحكم المتقن ممن لا حياة له ولا علم ولا قدرة. والمجوس أنكروا ذلك. وهو أثبت الله تعالى شركاء غير أحياء لا علماء ولا قادرين والمجوس لم يجوزوا ذلك. والثالث: أنه جعل صنع كل جماد وموات وأكثر من صنع الله تعالى، لأن الله تعالى لم يخلق إلا الأجسام ثم كل جسم خلقه يخلق إما باختياره وإما بالطبع ما لا يحصى من الأعراض، فيكون بمقابلته كل فرد من أجسام العالم الذي تولى الله تعالى تخليقه ما لا يحصى كثرة مما لا يخلقه الله تعالى. والرابع: أن المجوس ما أضافوا إلى غير الصانع الحكيم إلا الشرور والقبائح تنزيها له، وهو كما أضاف الشرور والقبائح من الموت والسقم والمرض والزمانة والعمى والصم والعرج والشلل إلى غير الله تعالى أضاف أيضا المحاسن والخيرات من الفرح والسرور واللذة والحياة والصحة والبصر والسمع إلى غير الله تعالى، فضاهى المجوس في إضافة الشرور إلى غير الله تعالى، وأربى عليهم بإضافة الخيرات والمحاسن إلى غير الله.
First: that the Magians affirm for the Maker only one partner, while he affirmed partners beyond count. Second: that he permitted the existence of perfect, precise action from one who has no life, no knowledge, and no power. The Magians denied that. And he affirmed for Allah partners that are not living, not knowing, not powerful, while the Magians did not allow that. Third: that he made the making of every inanimate and dead thing and more than the making of Allah Almighty, because Allah Almighty did not create except the bodies, then each body He created generates either by its choice or by nature countless accidents, so corresponding to every single body of the world whose creation Allah Almighty undertook are countless things that Allah does not create. Fourth: that the Magians did not attribute to other than the Wise Maker except evils and ugly things, to exalt Him, while he, just as he attributed evils and ugly things like death, illness, disease, chronic disability, blindness, deafness, lameness, and paralysis to other than Allah, also attributed good things and blessings like joy, happiness, pleasure, life, health, sight, and hearing to other than Allah. Thus he matched the Magians in attributing evils to other than Allah, and surpassed them in attributing good things and blessings to other than Allah.
Source pages p. 890

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of four arguments demonstrating that the dualists (Ashāb al-Ithnayn) surpass the Magians (Zoroastrians) in error regarding the association of partners with Allah. The author lists each point sequentially. First, the Magians affirm only one partner for the Creator (i.e., Ahriman), while the dualists affirm countless partners. Second, the Magians reject the idea that a lifeless, ignorant, powerless being can produce a well-ordered action, but the dualists allow it, thus attributing partners to Allah who lack life, knowledge, and power. Third, the Magians do not claim that the world's inanimate objects produce more than Allah does, but the dualists claim that every body creates countless accidents, rivaling Allah's creation. Fourth, the Magians only attribute evils to other than the Creator to preserve His goodness, but the dualists also attribute goods (like joy, health) to other than Allah, exceeding the Magians in shirk.

Key Terms

الصانع
الشريك
الأعراض
الأجسام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the author is only criticizing Magians, but he is actually using Magians as a benchmark to condemn dualists more severely.
Correction: The passage explicitly compares dualists to Magians, showing that while Magians already commit shirk, the dualists' error is far greater in four specific ways.

Checkpoint
According to the author, in what way do the dualists surpass the Magians in the fourth point?
A) They attribute only evils to other than Allah.
B) They attribute both goods and evils to other than Allah.
C) They deny any creation other than Allah.
D) They affirm only one partner for the Creator.

Key Takeaway
The dualists commit a more severe shirk than the Magians by affirming countless partners, attributing actions to lifeless beings, claiming greater creation from partners, and attributing both good and evil to them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience a sudden joy or a success, does your heart instinctively thank your own effort or another person before turning to Allah? How does the fourth point about attributing goods to other than Allah expose that subtle shirk in your daily life? Commit to pausing and redirecting your gratitude entirely to Allah for one day.
?
The dualists claimed that inanimate objects produce actions by their nature. Do you ever subconsciously assign power to objects—like a lucky charm, a job title, or a habit—forgetting that Allah alone creates and sustains every effect? How can you actively dismantle that hidden reliance? Write down one object you tend to over-rely on and replace it with a dhikr of Allah's sole power.
?
The author uses the Magians as a benchmark, showing that even their limited shirk is condemned. If even a single partner is intolerable, what does it say about your heart when it hosts multiple 'partners' of worldly attachments? Which attachments are you still clinging to, and what would it cost you to remove them from the throne of your heart today?

Refuting Creators Among Creatures
Author refutes Bishr and Mu'tazila for making creatures creators, comparing them to Magians, and cites the hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the Mu'tazila claim that creatures create their own actions, demonstrating that it implies shirk and mirrors Magian dualism, and how the prophetic hadith applies to this doctrine.

Core Idea
Claiming creatures create their actions makes them partners with Allah, even animals.

This passage tackles a core theological dispute: do humans create their own actions? The Mu'tazila said yes, but the author shows how that premise leads to absurd consequences—making even fleas partners in creation. He then ties this to the prophetic warning that the Qadariyya are the Magians of this community, highlighting the danger of attributing creative power to creatures.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two arguments
The passage first refutes Bishr's view that humans can create accidents like color and taste, then refutes the majority Mu'tazila view that all voluntary actions are created by creatures. Notice the reductio ad absurdum that even animals become partners.
The author uses a logical consequence to show the absurdity.
2
Analyze the comparison to Magians
The author says the Mu'tazila imitated the Magians and surpassed them in two ways (explained earlier). Consider what dualism means and why this comparison is severe.
Magians believed in two creators—good and evil. The Mu'tazila multiply creators infinitely.
3
Reflect on the hadith and its application
The Prophet said, 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this community.' Understand how this hadith applies specifically to those who attribute creation of actions to creatures, not just those who deny destiny.
The hadith is a strong condemnation linking theological error to shirk.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبشر بن المعتمر أحد رؤسائهم يجوز خلق اللون والطعم والرائحة والبصر والسمع والإدراك من غير الله تعالى، فيصير خالق هؤلاء شركاء الله تعالى في تخليق العالم. وجمهور المعتزلة يجعلون كل فعل حصل من أحد المخلوقين الأحياء باختيارهم مخلوقاً لهم خارجاً عن مقدور الله تعالى، فيكون كل كلب وخنزير وبق وبعوض شريكاً للمتعالي في العالم بعضه له ما لا قدرة الله عليه وبعضه الله تعالى، فيذهب كل منهم بما خلق، وهؤلاء الجمهور منهم بل كلهم ضاهوا المجوس وأربوا عليهم بوجهين على ما قررنا في إبطال كلام معمر، ولهذا ورد المأثور عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم "القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة". وإنما قلنا: إن مذهبهم يؤدي إلى القول بكون قدرته من صفات الفعل، وذلك
And Bishr ibn al-Muʿtamir, one of their leaders, permits the creation of color, taste, smell, sight, hearing, and perception from other than Allah Almighty, so the creators of these become partners with Allah Almighty in the creation of the world. And the majority of the Muʿtazila make every action that occurs from any living creature by their choice a creation of theirs, outside the power of Allah Almighty. Thus every dog, pig, flea, and mosquito becomes a partner of the Most High in the world—a part of it belongs to that which Allah has no power over, and a part to Allah Almighty—and each goes off with what it created. These majority—indeed all of them—imitated the Magians and surpassed them in two ways, as we established in refuting the speech of Muʿammar. For this reason, the transmitted report from the Prophet (peace be upon him) has come: 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this community.' And we only say that their doctrine leads to the statement that His power is among the attributes of action, and that...
Source pages p. 891

Commentary
This passage refutes two groups within the Muʿtazila. First, it mentions Bishr ibn al-Muʿtamir, who held that accidents like color, taste, etc., can be created by humans through generated acts (tawallud). This makes those humans partners with Allah in creation. Second, the majority of Muʿtazila hold that every voluntary action of a living being is created by that being, outside Allah's power. The author uses a reductio ad absurdum: this would make even lowly animals like dogs and fleas partners with Allah in parts of the world over which Allah has no power. The author then states that these Muʿtazila have emulated the Magians and surpassed them in two ways (as previously explained in the refutation of Muʿammar). He then cites the prophetic hadith: 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this community.' Finally, he begins a concluding statement that their doctrine leads to making Allah's power an attribute of action (not essence), implying innovation.

Key Terms
بشر بن المعتمر
المعتزلة
خلق الأفعال
القدرية
مجوس هذه الأمة
صفات الفعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith 'Qadariyya are Magians' only applies to those who deny divine destiny entirely (qadar).
Correction: The author applies it specifically to those who attribute creation of actions to creatures, showing it includes the Mu'tazila position.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the consequence of the Mu'tazila's view that creatures create their own actions?
A) Only humans become partners with Allah.
B) Even animals become partners with Allah in parts of creation.
C) Allah's power is limited to essential attributes only.
D) The Magians are absolved of shirk.

Key Takeaway
Attributing creation of actions to creatures inevitably implies shirk and mirrors Magian dualism, as warned by the Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what areas of your life do you unconsciously act as if your choices and actions are completely independent of Allah's will? What would change if you truly believed that every action you take is created by Allah alone?
?
The author uses lowly animals like dogs and fleas to show the absurdity of creatures being creators. When you feel proud of your achievements, do you ever think you created them yourself? How can you remind yourself that all success is from Allah?
?
Imagine the Prophet ﷺ calling you from the Qadariyya. Do you see any trace in your heart that claims ownership over your deeds? What step will you take today to return all agency to Allah?

Refutation of Mu'tazilite Claim on Miracles
Refutes two Mu'tazilite positions on miracles and creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidites consider the Mu'tazilite view on miracles as unbelief and how Bishr's view of human creation leads to shirk.

Core Idea
Denying God's creation of miracles leads to shirk.

In this passage, the Maturidi theologian refutes two related Mu'tazilite arguments. First, he condemns the claim that miraculous events are mere accidents not created by God, calling it unbelief. Then, he points out the extreme position of Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir, who allows humans to create certain attributes, effectively making them partners with God.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the literal English translation. Note the list of miracles and attributes mentioned.
The author uses a concise style; each item is a reference to a well-known prophetic miracle.
2
Identify the two claims being refuted
The passage addresses two distinct Mu'tazilite positions. Locate the first claim (general Mu'tazilite view) and the second claim (Bishr's specific view).
The transition word 'و' introduces the second claim.
3
Understand why the first claim is kufr
The author states that attributing miracles to accidents without God's creation is unbelief. Reflect on why denying God's direct creative power in miracles undermines tawhid.
The phrase 'لا صنع الله تعالى فيها' directly negates divine creation.
4
See how Bishr's view leads to shirk
Bishr permits creation of color, taste, etc., from other than Allah. The author concludes this makes humans partners in creation. Consider how this violates the unique creative power of Allah.
The term 'شركاء الله' explicitly accuses Bishr of shirk.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يثبت في العصا من الجيئة والذهاب، وفي اليد من النور، وفي الماء من الانفلاق، وفي الميت من الحياة، وفي الأكمة والأبرص من البرء، وفي الخشب من الحنين، وفي الشاه المسمومة من الكلام كل ذلك أعراض لا صنع الله تعالى فيها، والقول به كفر. وبشر بن المعتمر أحد رؤسائهم يجوز خلق اللون والطعم والرائحة والبصر والسمع والإدراك من غير الله تعالى، فيصير خالق هؤلاء شركاء الله تعالى في تخليق العالم.
It is affirmed in the stick of coming and going, and in the hand of light, and in the water of splitting, and in the dead of life, and in the blind and leper of healing, and in the wood of longing, and in the poisoned sheep of speech — all of these are accidents (a'rad) in which God Almighty has no creative act, and holding this view is unbelief (kufr). And Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir, one of their leaders, permits the creation of color, taste, smell, sight, hearing, and perception from other than God Almighty, so the creator of these becomes a partner with God Almighty in the creation of the world.
Source pages p. 891

Commentary
This passage refutes two related Mu'tazilite positions. First, the author mentions that the Mu'tazilites affirm the miraculous attributes in the stories of the prophets (such as the movement of Moses' staff, the light from his hand, the splitting of the sea, the reviving of the dead, healing of the blind and leper, the wood's longing, and the speech of the poisoned sheep) but claim these are mere accidents (a'rad) that God did not create. The author declares this position as kufr (unbelief). Second, he singles out Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir, a leading Mu'tazilite, who goes further by claiming that humans can create colors, tastes, smells, sight, hearing, and perception through generated causation (tawallud). This would make humans creators and thus partners with God in creating the world. The author presents this as an even more egregious error.

Key Terms

صنع الله
كفر
بشر بن المعتمر
شركاء الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think Mu'tazilites deny miracles entirely, but they affirm the miraculous attributes while denying God's direct creation of them.
Correction: The Mu'tazilites do not deny the occurrence of miracles; they reinterpret them as accidents that God did not create directly. The author refutes this by declaring it unbelief.

Checkpoint

A) It is permissible (ja'iz)
B) It is disliked (makruh)
C) It is unbelief (kufr)
D) It is obligatory (wajib)

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite denial of God's creative role in miracles is unbelief, and Bishr's permission for humans to create attributes is shirk.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience a blessing or a difficulty, do you see it as directly from God's hand, or do you attribute it to natural causes or your own efforts? How does this lesson challenge you to see every event as God's creation?
?
Are there areas of your life where you act as if you are the creator of your own abilities or character, forgetting that even your perception and attributes are from God? What step can you take today to acknowledge God's sole creative power?
?
If holding that God does not directly create miracles is kufr, what about your daily attitude towards God's involvement in your life? Do you live as if God is the direct creator of every moment, or do you functionally attribute things to other causes? How will you change that starting today?

Mu'tazilite View Makes Creatures Partners with God
Logical refutation of Mu'tazilite belief in creature-created actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Mu'tazilite belief that creatures create their own actions logically implies that every creature is a partner with God, and why this is compared to Magian dualism.

Core Idea
If creatures create their own actions, they become partners with God in the world.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi presents a sharp logical refutation of the majority Mu'tazilite position on human action. He shows that if every living creature truly creates its own voluntary actions, then those actions fall outside God's power — making every dog, pig, and mosquito a partner with God in creation. This leads to a startling comparison with Magian dualism and explains a famous prophetic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to grasp the flow of the argument.
Notice how the author uses a strong logical consequence (fa-yakūnu...).
2
Identify the Mu'tazilite claim
Find the statement describing what the Mu'tazilites believe about human actions. Key: they say actions are created by the creature, outside God's power.
The phrase 'khārijan 'an maqdūri Llāh' is crucial.
3
Trace the logical implication
Understand why this leads to partnership: if creatures create actions God cannot create, they share in divine creative power.
The author enumerates lowly creatures to highlight the absurdity.
4
Examine the comparison to Magians
The author says the Mu'tazilites resemble the Magians (dualists) and even exceed them in two ways. Reflect on why this comparison is made and how the hadith supports it.
The hadith 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this nation' ties the argument to prophetic authority.
5
Reflect on the lesson for tawhid
Consider how this refutation defends tawhid (God's oneness) by affirming that all power and creation belong solely to Allah.
This is a central issue in the debate on free will and predestination.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجمهور المعتزلة يجعلون كل فعل حصل من أحد المخلوقين الأحياء باختيارهم مخلوقا لهم خارجا عن مقدور الله تعالى، فيكون كل كلب وخنزير وبق وبعوض شريكًا للمتعالي في العالم بعضه له ما لا قدرة الله عليه وبعضه الله تعالى، فيذهب كل منهم بما خلق، وهؤلاء الجمهور منهم بل كلهم ضاهوا المجوس وأربوا عليهم بوجهين على ما قررنا في إبطال كلام معمر، ولهذا ورد المأثور عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم "القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة".
And the majority of the Mu'tazilites make every action that occurs from one of the living creatures by their choice created by them, outside the power (maqdur) of God Almighty, so every dog, pig, gnat, and mosquito becomes a partner with the Most High in the world — part of it for them, that over which God has no power, and part for God Almighty. Each of them goes off with what they created. These of the majority, indeed all of them, resemble the Magians and exceed them in two respects, as we have established in refuting the speech of Mu'ammar. For this reason, the transmitted saying from the Prophet (peace be upon him) has come: 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this nation.'
Source pages p. 891

Commentary
This passage presents the author's second refutation of the Mu'tazilite view on human action. He states that the majority of Mu'tazilites hold that every voluntary action of a living creature is created by that creature itself, outside the power (maqdur) of God. This logically implies that every creature — even a dog, pig, gnat, or mosquito — is a partner (sharik) with God in the world, since part of the world's actions are beyond God's power. The author then compares the Mu'tazilites to the Magians (majus), who believed in two creators, and claims the Mu'tazilites surpass them in two respects (as earlier explained in his refutation of Mu'ammar). To support this, he quotes the famous hadith: 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this nation.' The Qadariyya here refers to those who deny God's creation of human actions, i.e., the Mu'tazilites.

Key Terms
مقدور
شريك
المجوس
القدرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith 'Qadariyya are the Magians' refers to predestinarians (those who believe in predestination).
Correction: In this passage, the Qadariyya are those who deny God's creation of human actions and attribute creation to creatures, i.e., the Mu'tazilites, not predestinarians.

Checkpoint
What does the hadith cited in this passage say about the Qadariyya?
A) They are the best of this nation
B) They are the Magians of this nation
C) They will enter Paradise
D) They are forgiven

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite view that creatures create their own actions logically implies they are partners with God, a notion refuted by the Prophetic hadith comparing them to Magians.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, when you succeed at something, do you immediately think 'I did that' while forgetting that even your ability to act was gifted by God? How can you train yourself to see God's hand in every action you take?
?
The Prophet equated attributing creation to creatures with the dualism of the Magians. In what subtle ways do you give credit to yourself or others for what only God can create, such as your character, achievements, or even your faith?
?
If you truly believed that every action—good or bad—is created by God, how would that change the way you view your mistakes? Would you still feel shame or blame yourself, or would it lead you to deeper reliance on God's mercy?

Al-Ka'bi's Objection on Action Similarity
Al-Ka'bi presents his objection against those who affirm similarity of actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ka'bi's objection that those who claim to do the very action of God are more liable to the charge of similarity than those who merely claim to do its like.

Core Idea
Al-Ka'bi turns the charge of similarity by accusing opponents of identity, not mere likeness.

Al-Ka'bi, a Mu'tazili theologian, objects to those who say they do the like of God's action. He argues that his own group merely claims likeness, while his opponents claim actual identity, making them more deserving of the accusation that their actions resemble God's. This objection forces a careful distinction between types of action attribution.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection passage
Read the Arabic passage once and then its translation. Notice how al-Ka'bi frames the objection as a hypothetical from his opponents.
The passage is short but contains a logical argument.
2
Identify the two claims
Find the two claims: 'doing the like of our Lord's action' and 'doing the very action of your Lord'. Notice that al-Ka'bi attributes the first to his own group and the second to his opponents.
3
Understand the logic
Al-Ka'bi argues that claiming identity is more problematic than claiming mere likeness. Why? Because identity implies a stronger resemblance. Ask yourself: which position is more vulnerable to the charge of similarity?
This sets up the need for a distinction between types of action attribution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا اعتراض الكعبي ذكر في المقالات فإن قالوا إنا إن قلنا: إنا نفعل مثل فعل ربنا، ولكن لا شك أن فعلنا غير فعل ربنا وإنكم تزعمون أنكم تفعلون عين فعل ربكم فأنتم أحق بالقول باشتباه فعلكم بفعل ربكم. قلنا لهم: أما الأشعرية وأبو عيسى البرغوث من النجارية فإنهم إن زعموا أن الفعل عين المفعول فإنهم يأبون أن يكون العبد فاعلاً فلا يستقيم قولكم في حقهم إنكم تفعلون فعل ربكم، فسقط كلامكم في حقهم. ومن قال من النجارية ومتكلمي أهل الحديث: أن العبد يفعل إلا أن فعله الاكتساب لما أحدثه الله تعالى لا الإحداث فهؤلاء وإن قرروا بالفعل ولكن فعلهم ليس بخلق فلم يكونوا خلقوا كخلق الله تعالى وأنتم الخالقون بزعمكم كخلق الله تعالى؛ فلزمكم هذا الكلام وسقط عنهم.
This is the objection of al-Kaʿbī mentioned in al-Maqālāt. If they say: 'We say that we do the like of our Lord's action, but there is no doubt that our action is other than our Lord's action, while you claim that you do the very action of your Lord, so you are more deserving of saying that your action resembles your Lord's action.' We say to them: As for the Ashʿarīs and Abū ʿĪsā al-Barghūth from the Najjārīs, if they claim that the act (al-fiʿl) is identical to the effect (al-mafʿūl), then they deny that the servant is an agent (fāʿil), so your statement that 'you do the action of your Lord' does not apply to them, so your speech fails regarding them. And as for those from the Najjārīs and the theologians of the Ahl al-Ḥadīth who say that the servant does act, but that his action is acquisition (iktisāb) for what Allah has originated, not origination (īḥdāth), these, even if they are affirmed as acting, their action is not creation (khalq), so they are not creators like Allah's creation, while you are creators according to your claim like Allah's creation; so this speech applies to you and is removed from them.
Source pages p. 897

Commentary
This passage records an objection from al-Kaʿbī and Nasafi's response. Al-Kaʿbī argues that if someone says 'we do the like of our Lord's action' while admitting that our action is different from God's, then those who claim to do the very same action as God (i.e., the opponents) are more deserving of the charge of similarity (ishtibāh). Nasafi responds by distinguishing among theological groups: (1) The Ashʿarīs and Abū ʿĪsā al-Barghūth (a Najjārī) hold that the act is identical to the effect, and they deny that the servant is an agent (fāʿil). Therefore, al-Kaʿbī's statement that they 'do the action of their Lord' does not apply to them, since they do not attribute action to the servant. (2) The Najjārīs and the theologians of Ahl al-Ḥadīth who affirm that the servant acts but that his action is acquisition (iktisāb) of what Allah originates, not origination itself—these theologians also avoid the charge because their action is not creation (khalq); they do not liken themselves to Allah's creative act. In contrast, al-Kaʿbī's group (the Muʿtazila) claim that the servant creates like Allah's creation, so the objection about similarity actually applies to them, not to the Ashʿarīs or the Ahl al-Ḥadīth.

Key Terms
الكعبي
الاشتراك في الفعل
الفعل
الرب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ka'bi is admitting that his own group is guilty of similarity.
Correction: Al-Ka'bi is using the objection to argue that his opponents are more deserving of the charge, not that his own group is innocent.

Checkpoint
What does al-Ka'bi claim his opponents do?
A) They do the like of God's action.
B) They do the very action of God.
C) They deny that humans act at all.
D) They claim that human action is created by God.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ka'bi's objection highlights that claiming identity of action with God is more problematic than claiming mere likeness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever claimed to do something 'just like God'—perhaps in a moment of pride after a good deed? How does this passage expose the danger of that thought in your own heart?
?
When you see others committing a fault, do you unconsciously magnify their error while downplaying a similar fault in yourself? How does al-Ka'bi turning the tables challenge you to examine your own accusations?
?
This lesson shows a theological argument about divine actions. But in your daily life, do you ever treat your actions as if they have the same weight or finality as God's decrees? What would it look like to repent of that subtle self-deification?

Nasafi's Refutation: Action as Acquisition vs. Creation
Nasafi refutes al-Ka'bi's objection by surveying different theological positions on human action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi refutes al-Ka'bi's objection by showing that different theological schools avoid the charge of similarity through distinct understandings of human action.

Core Idea
Nasafi turns the charge back: only Mu'tazila claim human creation; others affirm acquisition without creation.

In response to al-Ka'bi's objection, Nasafi provides a nuanced refutation. He distinguishes between the Ash'ari position (denying human agency altogether), the Najjari and Ahl al-Hadith position (affirming action as acquisition of God's creation), and the Mu'tazili position (affirming human creation). He argues that al-Ka'bi's charge only applies to the Mu'tazila themselves, who claim their actions are creative like God's.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that Nasafi addresses two groups in his response.
The passage is a single continuous argument.
2
Identify the three theological positions
Nasafi mentions the Ash'aris and Abu Isa al-Barghuth, the Najjaris and Ahl al-Hadith, and implicitly the Mu'tazila. For each, note their view on the nature of human action.
The Mu'tazila are addressed indirectly as 'antum' (you).
3
Understand why the charge fails for Ash'aris
Ash'aris deny that the servant is an agent at all, so al-Ka'bi's claim that they 'do the action of their Lord' does not apply.
4
Understand why the charge fails for Najjaris/Ahl al-Hadith
They affirm human action but define it as acquisition (iktisab) of what Allah originates, not origination itself. Thus their action is not creation (khalq), so they do not liken themselves to God's creative act.
Nasafi concludes that the charge applies to the Mu'tazila, who claim to create like God.

?

?

?
Nasafi refutes the charge of similarity by affirming that acquisition does not make one a creator. Is there a part of your faith life where you confuse your religious deeds with 'earning' God's favor as if you were the originator? How can you live today with the peace that even your obedience is a gift you acquire from Him?

The Flaw in the Objection of Similarity
Refutation of Mu'tazilite objection using their own premise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the Mu'tazilite objection by exposing their own inconsistency and the impossibility of similarity when acts are identified.

Core Idea
Similarity requires two distinct things, so the objection self-destructs.

The Mu'tazila argue that if human acts are similar to divine acts, the distinction collapses. The author shows that their own framework—where acts are distinct—actually implies two similar acts exist, thus admitting divine creation in human acts. Then he shows that for those who identify the acts, similarity is impossible. This lesson unpacks the logical steps of this refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the flow from critiquing the Mu'tazila to discussing the Najjariyya view.
2
Identify the two claims made against the Mu'tazila
First, the author points out that similarity requires two things, and the Mu'tazila admit two similar movements. Second, for those who say acts are identical, similarity is impossible. Understand each point.
3
Connect to the broader argument
Ask yourself: Why does the author bring up the Najjariyya and hadith theologians? It shows that even if one accepts the servant has an act, the objection fails.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومما يكشف عن عوار هذا الكلام أن الاشتباه يجري بين شيئين، وعندكم فعلكم غير فعل الله تعالى فكانت إحدى الحركتين عندكم فعل العبد والأخرى فعل الله تعالى وهما متشابهتان، فوجد منكم على زعمكم خلق كخلق الله تعالى، فأما عندنا من يسلم لكم من النجارية ومتكلمي أهل الحديث أن العبد له فعل ففعله عندهم عين فعل الله تعالى، فهو من حيث إنه خلق فعل الله تعالى ومن حيث إنه حركة أو سكون طاعة أو معصية فعل العبد، فعين الكسب هو عين الخلق، وعين الخلق هو عين الكسب، كما أن عين الحركة هو عين الشيء وعين الشيء هو عين الحركة وإثبات الاشتباه في شيء واحد محال إذ الشيء لا يشبه نفسه، فكان إلزامكم إياهم فاسد. فعل الله خلق وإيجاد وفعل العبد مباشرة واكتساب] وعندنا فعل العبد وإن كان غير فعل الله إلا أن فعل الله تعالى خلق وإيجاد وفعلنا مباشرة واكتساب فلم يلزم التشابه، والله الموفق.
And among what reveals the defect of this speech is that similarity occurs between two things. According to you, your act is not the act of God Almighty, so one of the two movements according to you is the act of the servant and the other is the act of God Almighty, and they are similar. So according to your claim, there came from you a creation like the creation of God Almighty. As for us, those who concede to you among the Najjariyya and the speculative theologians of the hadith people that the servant has an act, their view is that his act is the very act of God Almighty. So it is, insofar as it is creation, the act of God Almighty, and insofar as it is movement or stillness, obedience or disobedience, the act of the servant. Thus the very acquisition (al-kasb) is the very creation, and the very creation is the very acquisition, just as the very movement is the very thing and the very thing is the very movement. Proving similarity in a single thing is impossible, for a thing does not resemble itself. Therefore your inference against them is invalid. The act of God is creation and bringing into existence, and the act of the servant is direct performance and acquisition. And according to us, the act of the servant, even if it is other than the act of God, yet the act of God Almighty is creation and bringing into existence, and our act is direct performance and acquisition, so similarity does not necessarily follow. And God is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 898

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection concerning the similarity between divine and human acts. The author begins by identifying the flaw in the opponent's argument: similarity (al-ishtibah) can only occur between two distinct things. According to the Mu'tazilite opponents, the servant's act is not God's act, but they claim two movements are similar—one from the servant, one from God. So they themselves admit an instance of creation like God's creation. The author then contrasts this with the view of the Najjariyya and some hadith theologians who hold that the servant's act is identical to God's act in creation, differing only in kasb (acquisition). In their view, the act is both God's creation and the servant's acquisition. Thus, similarity does not apply because it is one thing. The author then clarifies his own position: the servant's act is distinct from God's act—God creates and brings into existence, while the servant directly performs and acquires. Since the acts differ in essence, no similarity arises. The passage ends with an invocation for divine assistance.

Key Terms
اشتباه (ishtibah, similarity)
خلق (khalq, creation)
كسب (kasb, acquisition)
فعل (fi'l, act)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author agrees with the Najjariyya that human and divine acts are identical.
Correction: The author cites their view only to show the inconsistency of the Mu'tazilite objection. His own position, stated later, distinguishes the acts in essence.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why does the Mu'tazilite objection fail?
A) Because similarity requires two distinct things, and the Mu'tazila only have one act.
B) Because the Mu'tazila admit similarity between two distinct acts, but for those who identify the acts, similarity is impossible.
C) Because the Najjariyya deny that the servant has any act.
D) Because the author denies any similarity between divine and human acts.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite objection fails because it either admits similarity between distinct acts (contradicting their own premise) or reduces to impossibility when acts are identified.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author exposes a contradiction in the Mu'tazilite position: they admit similarity between distinct acts, which implies a creation like God's. Have you ever held a belief that, if examined honestly, contradicts your own foundational principles? Will you take time today to identify one such inconsistency in your thinking about God's actions and your own?
?
The Najjariyya equate the servant's act with God's act, yet the passage does not endorse this view—it only uses it to refute the objection. Are you tempted to oversimplify the relationship between divine sovereignty and human responsibility to avoid theological tension? How might this be a form of intellectual laziness rather than true faith?
?
The argument hinges on the fact that a thing cannot resemble itself. When you look at your own actions, do you secretly separate them from God's will in a way that makes you feel independent? This passage calls you to confront whether you truly live as though your every movement is both God's creation and your acquisition—or do you resort to one side only when convenient?

The Maturidi Distinction: Creation vs. Acquisition
Statement of Maturidi distinction between divine and human acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi view that divine acts are creation (khalq) and bringing into existence (ījād), while human acts are direct performance (mubāshara) and acquisition (kasb), and why this avoids similarity.

Core Idea
God creates the act; the human acquires and performs it.

After refuting the objection, the author presents his own positive doctrine: there is no real similarity because the nature of the act differs. God's act is creation and bringing into existence, while the servant's act is direct performance and acquisition. This distinction resolves the problem without conflating divine and human agency. In this lesson, we examine the key terms and the logical conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the key terms
Read the Arabic and translation. Identify the four key terms: khalq (creation), ījād (bringing into existence), mubāshara (direct performance), kasb (acquisition).
These terms are central to Maturidi theology.
2
Understand the two aspects of the act
The author says the act of God is khalq and ījād; our act is mubāshara and kasb. Notice that the act is one but has two different aspects depending on the agent.
3
Apply the conclusion
Since the divine and human acts differ in essence (creation vs. acquisition), similarity does not arise. Reflect on how this preserves both divine omnipotence and human responsibility.

Clarifying the Mu'tazila's Claim on One Act Under Two Powers
Author dissects the Mu'tazila's claim by asking what they mean by impossibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author critically examines the Mu'tazila's claim that one act cannot be under two powers, by distinguishing between creation (ikhtirāʿ) and acquisition (kasb).

Core Idea
Not all impossibility is the same—the Mu'tazila confused creation with acquisition.

The Mu'tazila argued that it is impossible for one act to be under two powers. But what exactly do they mean by 'impossible'? The author pins them down by asking: do you mean from the aspect of creation, acquisition, or both? This lesson walks through the dialectic and shows that the only real dispute is about the combination of divine creation and human acquisition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Notice the author's dialectical style.
The passage is a direct address to the Mu'tazila, so it reads like a debate.
2
Identify the three interpretations
The author offers three interpretations of 'impossible': from creation alone, from acquisition alone, or from both. Find these in the text.
3
Understand the author's concessions
Note that the author concedes impossibility for creation (two creators) and acquisition (two acquirers) separately. Why does he concede these?
These concessions show he agrees with the Mu'tazila on certain points.
4
Locate the real dispute
The author identifies the dispute as the combination of creation and acquisition—one act created by God and acquired by a human. This is the point the Mu'tazila deny.
5
Reflect on the rebuke
The author accuses the Mu'tazila of ignorance for considering the possible impossible. Ask yourself: why does he consider their position dogmatic?
This step connects to the broader theme of rational inquiry in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قيل لهم أيش تعنون بقولكم إن دخول مقدور واحد تحت قدرة قاردين محال ؟ أتعنون دخوله من جهة الاختراع أو من جهة الاكتساب أو من جهة اكتساب و اختراع؟ فإن قالوا من جهة الاختراع فسلم تنازعهم في هذا ، وإن قالوا: من جهة الاكتساب فكذلك لأن فعلاً واحدًا لا يكون فعلا لكاسبين. وإن (۳) قالوا من جهة الاكتساب والاختراع أن (٤) يقدر على اختراعه مخترع وعلى اكتسابه مكتسب ففيه النزاع. فقيل لهم : لم قلتم ذلك وقد وقعت الخصومة فيه ثم ما أقمنا من الدلائل موجب ذلك ومن عد الممكن ممتنعا فهو جاهلي فكيف بمن عد الواجب ممتنعا؟ ثم هم إنما عدوا ذلك ممتنعا لأنهم لم يعقلوا تعلق القدرة بالمقدور إلا من جهة الاختراع وذلك لعمري ،محال وعند خصومهم قط لا يجوز تعلق قدرتين بجهة الاختراع بمقدور واحد وإنما الكلام وراء ذلك وهو أن قدرة واحدة لما تعلقت
Then it was said to them: What do you mean by your statement that the entry of one act of power under the power of two powers is impossible? Do you mean its entry from the aspect of creation (ikhtirāʿ), or from the aspect of acquisition (kasb), or from the aspect of acquisition and creation? If they say: from the aspect of creation, then we concede the dispute to them in this. And if they say: from the aspect of acquisition, then likewise, because one act cannot be an act for two acquirers. And if they say: from the aspect of acquisition and creation – that a creator (mukhtariʿ) can create it and an acquirer (muktasib) can acquire it – then therein lies the dispute. So it was said to them: Why do you say that, when the dispute has occurred regarding it, and then we have established proofs necessitating that? And whoever considers the possible impossible is ignorant, so how about one who considers the impossible impossible? Then they only considered that impossible because they did not conceive of the attachment of power to the act of power except from the aspect of creation – and that, by my life, is impossible. And according to their opponents, the attachment of two powers to one act from the aspect of creation is never permissible. Rather, the discussion is beyond that, which is that one power when it attaches...
Source pages p. 906

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical analysis of the Mu'tazila's claim that one act cannot be under two powers. The author presents a precise question: what exactly do they mean by 'impossible'? He offers three interpretations: (a) impossibility from the aspect of creation (ikhtirāʿ), (b) impossibility from the aspect of acquisition (kasb), or (c) impossibility from both aspects. For (a), the author concedes: it is indeed impossible for two creators to create one act. For (b), he also concedes: one act cannot be the act of two acquirers (i.e., two human agents cannot both acquire the same act simultaneously). For (c), the combination of creation and acquisition – that a creator creates it and an acquirer acquires it – that is the real point of dispute. The author then rebukes the Mu'tazila for denying this possibility despite the existence of proofs. He accuses them of ignorance: calling something possible impossible. He states that they only considered it impossible because they only conceive of power attaching to an act from the aspect of creation, whereas their opponents also admit that two powers cannot attach from the aspect of creation. The real discussion lies elsewhere – namely, that a single power attaches to an act in a manner that allows for both divine creation and human acquisition. The passage ends mid-sentence, continuing the explanation.

Key Terms
اختراع
اكتساب
مخترع
مكتسب
تعلق القدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila believe that one act under two powers is absolutely impossible in every sense.
Correction: The author shows that it is only impossible when both powers are from the same aspect (both creators or both acquirers), but possible when one power creates and the other acquires.

Checkpoint
What does the author concede to the Mu'tazila?
A) That one act cannot be under two powers from the aspect of acquisition.
B) That one act can be under two powers from both aspects.
C) That their objection is entirely correct.
D) That the human is the true creator.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila's claim that one act cannot be under two powers is only accepted when both powers are from the same aspect (creation or acquisition), but the dispute lies in the combination of divine creation and human acquisition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever rejected a truth about Allah's actions simply because your mind couldn't fathom how it could be? How does this lesson challenge you to humble your intellect before His revelation—and what will you do about it today?
?
The author calls those who consider possible things impossible 'ignorant'. Where in your own life have you dismissed something as impossible—for yourself, for others, or for Allah—without having proper proof? What would it take for you to repent from that limitation?
?
The Mu'tazila confined Allah's power to their own conceptual framework. Where do you unintentionally confine His mercy, provision, or forgiveness to what you think is reasonable? What step can you take today to expand your trust in His unlimited capacity beyond your own understanding?

Three Options for the Opponent
Sanusi forces the opponent into a trilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three options Sanusi presents to the opponent and why they are unavoidable.

Core Idea
The opponent faces an inescapable trilemma.

Sanusi concludes his argument by turning the opponent's own reasoning against him. If the opponent rejects two agents acting together because it leads to absurdity, he must also reject two equal persons created by God. This forces the opponent into a choice among three unacceptable positions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice how Sanusi builds his argument with a conditional structure.
2
Identify the three options
List the three options Sanusi gives the opponent. Each corresponds to a different logical consequence.
The options are: retract on generated acts, allow two powers on one object, or be stubborn.
3
Reflect on the argument's force
Consider why these three options exhaust all possibilities. Ask yourself which option the opponent would prefer and why Sanusi considers them all unacceptable.
This shows the strength of the Sunni position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال له: إذا قلت يستحيل أن يتفق الاثنان على التحريك عند استوائهما في المعاني لأنه يؤدي إلى محال فقل يستحيل أن يخلق الله شخصين مستويي القدرة والبنية لأنه يؤدي إلى محال إذ لا فرق بينهما. ثم بعد ذلك إنك بين أمور ثلاثة: إما أن ترجع عن مسألة المتولدات وتجعلها الله تعالى كما هو مذهب أهل السنة، أو تجيز تعلق قدرتين بمقدور واحد وجعل شيء فعلاً لفاعلين وفيه رجوع عن مذهبك، أو تتمسك بالمذهبين مع لزوم الدليل فتوصف بالعناد المحض، والله الموفق.
Then it is said to him: When you say it is impossible for two to agree upon movement when they are equal in attributes because it leads to an absurdity, then say: It is impossible for God to create two persons equal in power and constitution because it leads to an absurdity, since there is no difference between them. Then after that, you are between three matters: either you retract from the issue of generated acts and make them [created] by God Almighty as is the doctrine of Ahl al-Sunna, or you allow the attachment of two powers to one object of power and make a thing an act of two agents, which involves retraction from your doctrine, or you adhere to both doctrines while the evidence necessitates [otherwise], so you are described as pure stubbornness. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 910

Commentary
This passage delivers a final argument against the opponent, forcing a choice among three positions. The author first turns the opponent's reasoning against him: if the opponent claims that two agents cannot agree on movement because it leads to an absurdity, then the opponent must also reject that God can create two equal persons, which he already accepted. Then the author lists three options. First: retract the view on generated acts (mutawallidat) and attribute all acts to God, which is the Sunni position. Second: allow two powers to be attached to one object of power (maqdur wahid), making an act belong to two agents—this would be a retraction from the opponent's own school. Third: stubbornly adhere to both contradictory doctrines, in which case the opponent is accused of pure obstinacy. The passage ends with a prayer for divine guidance.

Key Terms
المتولدات (generated acts)
تعلق قدرتين (attachment of two powers)
مقدور واحد (one object of power)
عناد (stubbornness)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The opponent can avoid all three options.
Correction: The three options exhaust all logical possibilities given the opponent's own premises.

Checkpoint
What is the first option the author presents to the opponent?
A) Accept two powers on one object
B) Retract on generated acts and attribute them to God
C) Adhere to both doctrines
D) Accuse the author of stubbornness

Key Takeaway
The opponent has no escape: he must either accept the Sunni position, contradict himself, or be stubborn.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are faced with a logical contradiction in your own beliefs, do you honestly retract and align with the truth, or do you cling to comfortable positions out of pride? Where in your life does the third option—pure stubbornness—threaten your integrity before Allah?
?
The opponent refused to apply his own reasoning to God, creating an inconsistency. Is there a belief you hold about God or His creation that you hesitate to follow to its logical conclusion because it would force you to change? What is stopping you from surrendering that inconsistency to the truth of Ahl al-Sunna?
?
Sanusi calls the opponent's third option 'pure stubbornness'. Which of your cherished opinions would you be willing to abandon today if the evidence of revelation and reason demanded it? Are you ready to pray for divine guidance to see your own blind spots?
