Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
6 min
Why God's Creation Does Not Imply Partnership
The author argues against the charge of shirk by analyzing the nature of partnership and ownership.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that God's complete ownership and exclusive creative power preclude any real partnership, using the examples of property and cooperative building.

Core Idea
True partnership requires exclusive ownership of parts; God's ownership of everything leaves no room for partners.

Having defined shirk, the author now refutes the notion that God's creation of human actions makes humans partners with God. He appeals to common understanding: partnership in property or labor requires each partner to have exclusive control over some part. But everything is owned by God in a real sense, and human actions depend entirely on God's creation of power. This lesson unpacks that logical argument.

Guided Path
1
Understand the customary definition of partnership
The author explains that in common language, partners in a village each own exclusive parts that others do not own.
This sets the standard for what counts as true partnership.
2
Apply to God and human property
Everything a servant owns is also owned by God as Creator; thus no exclusive ownership exists for the servant.
The author asserts that nothing leaves God's ownership.
3
Analyze the building analogy
Zayd and Amr are genuine partners because each contributes exclusive parts; but God creates the entire action and the power for it, leaving no part for the servant.
This highlights the disanalogy between human cooperation and God's sole creative power.

?

?

?

In which area of your life are you most tempted to claim exclusive ownership—your time, your money, your relationships? Will you commit to a concrete act that recognizes God’s sole ownership at the end of this lesson?

The True Nature of Shirk and Refuting the Accusation of Shirk
Definition of shirk and refutation of the charge of shirk against the orthodox view of human action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam al-Nasafi's definition of shirk as involving either worship of other than Allah or belief in another creator, and his argument that the orthodox view of human action does not entail shirk because ownership and power are not independent but derived.

Core Idea
Shirk is either in worship or in creation; the orthodox view of human action is not shirk because human power is granted by Allah.

Imam al-Nasafi begins by clarifying the true nature of shirk, distinguishing between two categories: shirk in worship and shirk in creation. He then addresses a common objection: does affirming that humans have power over their actions alongside Allah's power constitute shirk? Using an analogy from ownership, he demonstrates that simultaneous possession by two parties in different respects is not considered partnership by rational consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and English translation to get an overall sense of the argument.
2
Understand the two types of shirk
Notice that the first type (idolaters) acknowledges Allah as Creator but worships other beings; the second type is hypothetical shirk in creation.
3
Analyze the ownership analogy
The author argues that in customary language, partners own distinct portions exclusively. The same entity cannot be owned by two in the same respect.
4
Apply the analogy to power
God's power is original, human power is enabled by God. This is like ownership: God owns all creation, and humans own by grant. This is not partnership.
5
Conclude
The orthodox position does not imply shirk because power and ownership are not independent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والآخر من يثبت الله تعالى شريكا في استحقاق العبادة دون التخليق وهم عبدة الأصنام، فإنك إن سألتهم من خلق السماوات والأرض؟ ليقولن الله غير أنهم يعبدون الأصنام كما يعبدون الصانع، ويجعلونها مستحقة للعبادة كما استحقها الصانع ثم ما يوجد من عبادتهم للأصنام لا يكون عبادة الله تعالى وما يوجد من عبادتهم الله تعالى لا يكون عبادة للأصنام، وفي العرف عند أرباب اللسان الشركاء في القرية والمحلة قوم يكون كل واحد منهم اختص بملك شيء من القرية لا يملكه غيره من الشركاء، ولم يعقل كون شيء لذات من وجه ولذات من وجه شركة بينهما بإجماع العقلاء، فإن ما هو ملك العبد هو بعينه ملك لله تعالى ملك تخليق لم يزل شيء من المخلوقات عن ملكه بتملك العباد ذلك، ولم يقل أحد أن العبد شريك الله تعالى فمن ما يملكه من العقار أو الحيوان أو الثياب والفرش والأواني وغير ذلك، وإن كان ذلك ملك العبد وعين ما هو ملك العبد ملك الله تعالى، وعين ما ملك الله تعالى ملك العبد، ثم العالم أعراض وأعيان وما أوجده الله تعالى غير ما هو أوجده غيره، وما أوجده غيره غير ما أوجده الله تعالى فيكون العالم له ولأغياره، وهذا هو حقيقة الشركة. فأما ما قلنا فلا يوجب الشركة إذ عين ما هو مقدور الله تعالى مقدور العبد بإقداره، وما هو مقدور العبد مقدور الله تعالى، وهذا لا يعقل شركة كما في الملك إذ هو ما ملك العبد، عينه ملك الله وما هو ملك الله تعالى من الأعيان التي جعلها ملكًا لعباده عينه ملك العبد ولم يعد ذلك شركة في الملك بإجماع العقلاء.
And the other [type] is one who affirms a partner for God Almighty in deserving worship without [partnership in] creation, and they are the idolaters. For if you ask them: 'Who created the heavens and the earth?' they would say: 'God,' yet they worship idols as they worship the Maker, and they consider them deserving of worship as the Maker deserves it. Then what exists of their worship of idols is not worship of God Almighty, and what exists of their worship of God Almighty is not worship of idols. And in the custom of the people of language, the partners in a village or quarter are a people each of whom is distinguished by ownership of a part of the village which no other partner owns. And it is not rationally conceivable that a thing belong to an entity in one respect and to an entity in another respect be considered partnership between them by consensus of rational people. For what is the possession of the servant is exactly the possession of God Almighty - a possession of creation; nothing of created things has left His possession by the servants' possessing them. And no one has said that the servant is a partner of God Almighty because of what he owns of real estate, animals, clothes, furnishings, utensils, and other things, even though that is the possession of the servant, and exactly what is the possession of the servant is the possession of God Almighty, and exactly what God Almighty possesses is the possession of the servant. Then the world consists of accidents and substances. What God Almighty originated is other than what another originated, and what another originated is other than what God Almighty originated, so the world would belong to Him and to others, and that is the reality of partnership. As for what we say, it does not necessitate partnership, because exactly what is within the power of God Almighty is within the power of the servant by His enabling, and what is within the power of the servant is within the power of God Almighty. And this is not rationally conceivable as partnership, just as in ownership: what the servant owns, exactly it is the possession of God, and what is the possession of God Almighty of entities that He has made possessions for His servants is exactly the possession of the servant, and that is not considered partnership in ownership by consensus of rational people.
Source pages p. 939

Commentary
This passage combines a definition of shirk with a refutation of the accusation that the orthodox (Maturidi) view implies shirk. The author first distinguishes two types of shirk: shirk in worship (idolaters who acknowledge God as Creator but worship idols as partners in deserving worship) and shirk in creation (affirming another creator alongside God). He then uses an analogy from customary language: partners in a village each own distinct portions exclusively; if the same thing were owned by two persons in different respects, that is not called partnership by rational consensus. Applying this, the fact that God owns the same thing as a servant (God as Creator, servant as acquirer) does not constitute partnership, because God's ownership is original and the servant's is granted. No rational person calls such dual ownership 'partnership'. The author then reinforces that the world consists of accidents and substances; if another entity had originated something independently, that would be true shirk. Finally, he clarifies the orthodox position: God's power and the servant's power are not independent—the servant's power is an enabling from God, so the same act is within both powers without implying partnership, just as in ownership. The passage guards against the misunderstanding that affirming human acquisition (kasb) implies associating partners with God.

Key Terms
شركة
تخليق
ملك
قدرة
إقدار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God creates human actions and humans also acquire them, then both are partners in creation, which is shirk.
Correction: No, because human power is not independent; it is enabled by God. In the same way that a servant's ownership of property does not make him a partner with God in ownership, because God's ownership is original and the servant's is granted. The same applies to power.

Checkpoint
Which of the following does the author identify as constituting shirk?
A) Worshiping idols while acknowledging God as Creator
B) Ascribing a partner to God in creation
C) Both of the above
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
Shirk is defined as either partnering in worship or in creation; the orthodox view of human action does not constitute shirk because human power is derived from God, just as human ownership is derived from God's ownership.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The idolaters acknowledged God as Creator yet worshipped idols. Where in your life do you profess belief in God but still give your ultimate trust or devotion to something else—career, wealth, reputation? What would it take to uproot that hidden shirk?
?
You have probably accused others of wrongdoing or incorrect beliefs. This passage shows how careful the scholars were before labeling something shirk. When have you been quick to judge someone's Islamic practice without understanding their perspective? Will you commit to learning before accusing?
?
Everything you own—your house, your phone, your body—ultimately belongs to God. If you truly internalized that, how would your attachment to these things change? What one possession are you most unwilling to lose, and why?

The Mu'tazila Doctrine of Human Power Implies Shirk
Author uses partnership analogy to prove Mu'tazila doctrine entails shirk.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Mu'tazila view of human power leads to the conclusion that humans are partners with God in creation, according to the author.

Core Idea
Affirming independent human creativity makes every living being a partner of God.

In this passage, the author continues his critique of the Mu'tazila by showing that their doctrine of human power logically entails shirk. He uses the analogy of two partners building a house to illustrate how the combination of two independent powers results in partnership. This lesson traces that argument and the author's charge that the Mu'tazila, despite accusing others, are themselves guilty of associating partners with God.

Guided Path
1
Read the analogy of two builders
Start by reading the analogy of Zayd and Umar building a house together. Notice that each contributes according to his ability, and they are called partners.
The author uses a simple, everyday example to establish the meaning of partnership.
2
Apply the analogy to the Mu'tazila position
The author then applies this logic: if the servant creates his act and God creates the power, then the act results from both, making the servant a partner in every act. Identify how this leads to the conclusion that all living beings are partners in creation.
3
Examine the author's conclusion
Finally, read the conclusion where the author states that the Mu'tazila are the ones who affirm partners, and that their accusation against the orthodox is insolence or ignorance.
The author claims the orthodox position is free from shirk.

وكذا من كل فعل كأن العبد شريك الله، فإنا إذا رأينا أن زيدًا مع عمر إذا اشتركا في بناء الدار وما يقدر عليه هذا من أجزاء الدار لا يقدر عليه ذاك، وما يقدر عليه ذاك لا يقدر عليه هذا فجعل كل واحد منهما ما في قدرته حتى تم بناء الدار بهما لم يمتنع أحد من أرباب اللسان والعقلاء من القول زيدًا وعمر اشتركا في بناء الدار ثم إن الفعل من العبد لن يحصل إلا بوجود قدرة يخترعها الله تعالى لا قدرة للعبد عليها وفعل يخترعه العبد لا قدرة الله تعالى عليه وحصول الفعل بمجموع مقدوريهما، فكان الأحياء شركاء الله تعالى في تخليق العالم، وكل حي من كل فعل يفعله شريك الله تعالى. وبالوقوف على حقيقة الشركة علم أن المعتزلة هم الذين أثبتوا الله تعالى في العالم شركاء ومن كل فعل اختياري شريكا، ونحن بحمد الله تعالى برآء عن ذلك، فكانت نسبة المعتزلة إيانا إلى القول مما يوجب الشركة ووصف أنفسهم بالبراءة من ذلك وقاحة عظيمة أو جهلاً بحقيقة الشركة المعقولة، وصاروا بإثبات الشركاء الله تعالى في العالم وفي كل فعل مساعدين للمجوس بل كانوا شرا من المجوس من وجهين أحدهما أن المجوس ما أثبتوا الله إلا شريكاً واحدًا، وهؤلاء جعلوا كل ما دب ودرج من ذوي الأرواح والمهج شركاء الله تعالى. والثاني: أن المجوس أرادوا بإثبات الشريك تنزيه الله تعالى عما هو عندهم سفه، وما أضافوا إلى الشريك إلا الشرور والقبائح، والمعتزلة أضافوا كل ما هو حسن على الحقيقة إلى غير الله تعالى، وجعلوا ما فعله غيره أحسن مما فعله الله تعالى على ما قررنا والله العصمة والنجاة عن كل ضلالة وبدعة، وفي المسألة دلائل كثيرة ذكرها من تقدم من ائمتنا الماضين - قدس الله أرواحهم – ومن
And likewise, from every act it is as if the servant is a partner of God. For if we see that Zayd and Umar when they partnered in building a house, and what this one can do of the parts of the house that one cannot do, and what that one can do this one cannot do, so each of them being what is in his power until the building of the house is completed by both, no one among the people of language and rational people refrained from saying: 'Zayd and Umar partnered in building the house.' Then indeed, the act of the servant does not occur except by the existence of a power that God Almighty creates - no power over it for the servant - and an act that the servant creates - no power over it for God Almighty - and the occurrence of the act by the combination of what is within the power of both of them. So living beings would be partners of God Almighty in the creation of the world, and every living being from every act he does is a partner of God Almighty. And by understanding the reality of partnership, it is known that the Mu'tazila are the ones who affirmed for God Almighty partners in the world and from every voluntary act a partner. And we, by grace of God Almighty, are free from that. So the attribution of the Mu'tazila to us of the statement that necessitates partnership, and their description of themselves as free from that, is great insolence or ignorance of the rationally understood reality of partnership. And they, by affirming partners for God Almighty in the world and in every act, become helpers of the Magians, rather they are worse than the Magians in two respects: one is that the Magians only affirmed for God one partner, while these made every crawling and moving thing among the possessors of souls and life a partner of God Almighty. The second: that the Magians intended by affirming a partner to exonerate God Almighty from what they considered foolishness, and they only attributed to the partner evils and ugly things, while the Mu'tazila attributed everything that is truly good to other than God Almighty, and they made what another does better than what God Almighty does, as we have established. And God is the protector and salvation from every misguidance and innovation. And on this issue there are many proofs mentioned by those who preceded from our past imams - may God sanctify their spirits - and from
Source pages p. 939

Commentary
This passage builds on the preceding definition of shirk to argue that the Mu'tazila's doctrine actually entails shirk. The author first presents the Mu'tazila position (as he understands it) that human acts are created by human power alone, with God having no power over them. Using the analogy of two partners building a house—each contributes according to his ability and they are called partners—the author argues that if God creates a power that the servant uses, and the servant creates the act without God's power, then the act results from both powers, making the servant a partner with God in every act. Thus, the Mu'tazila view implies that every living being is a partner in the creation of the world. The author then explicitly states that the Mu'tazila are the ones who affirm partners for God, while the orthodox school is free from that. The Mu'tazila's accusation against the orthodox is either insolence or ignorance. The author further claims that the Mu'tazila are worse than the Magians (Zoroastrians) in two ways: first, the Magians only affirmed one partner (Ahriman), while the Mu'tazila multiply partners to every living being; second, the Magians only attributed evils to the partner, exonerating God from evil, while the Mu'tazila attribute truly good acts to other than God, implying that what humans do is better than what God does. The passage ends with a plea for divine protection and a reference to earlier imams for further proofs.

Key Terms
شركة
تخليق
قدرة
اختراع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The orthodox doctrine of kasb (acquisition) implies that humans are partners with God in creation.
Correction: The author argues that it is the Mu'tazila view, not the orthodox, that entails partnership, because it gives humans an independent creative power alongside God.

Checkpoint
What does the author conclude from the analogy of Zayd and Umar building a house?
A) That partnership requires equal contribution.
B) That the Mu'tazila position makes every living being a partner of God.
C) That the orthodox doctrine is correct.
D) That building a house requires divine assistance.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila belief that humans independently create their acts logically implies that every human is a partner with God in creation, which is shirk.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you accomplish something praiseworthy, do you ever secretly feel that your own skill or effort was the decisive factor, as if God's provision of ability was secondary? How does this passage expose that feeling as a form of hidden partnership? What will you do today to consciously attribute every result solely to Allah?
?
The Mu'tazila thought they were defending God's justice, but fell into shirk. Where in your own beliefs or practices might you be so focused on one truth about Allah that you inadvertently compromise another? Will you examine your heart tonight and ask Allah to purify your tawhid?
?
This passage says every living being becomes a partner of God if they claim independent power. Have you ever felt that your children, your possessions, or your health are 'yours' in a way that suggests they exist independently of Allah's continuous creation? How can you train your tongue and heart to constantly acknowledge that all creation is from Him alone?

The Mu'tazila Are Worse Than the Magians
Author enumerates two ways Mu'tazila are worse than Magians.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two reasons the author considers the Mu'tazila worse than the Magians (Zoroastrians) regarding the doctrine of partners for God.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila multiply partners and attribute good acts to them, surpassing the Magians in error.

After demonstrating that the Mu'tazila view implies shirk, the author takes his critique further by comparing them to the Magians (Zoroastrians). The Magians, according to the author, at least limited their dualism to one partner and assigned only evil to it. The Mu'tazila, however, multiply partners to every living being and attribute truly good acts to them, making their doctrine even more objectionable. This lesson explores that comparison.

Guided Path
1
Read the comparison introduction
Read the opening sentence where the author says the Mu'tazila become helpers of the Magians and are actually worse.
Note the phrase 'بل كانوا شرا من المجوس' – they are worse.
2
Identify the first reason
Find the first way: the Magians only affirmed one partner (Ahriman), while the Mu'tazila make every living being a partner.
This multiplies the partners infinitely.
3
Identify the second reason
Find the second way: the Magians only attributed evils to their partner, exonerating God from evil; but the Mu'tazila attribute truly good acts to other than God, implying those acts are better than God's.
This is a more fundamental insult to God's perfection.
4
Reflect on the charge
Consider the severity of this accusation: the Mu'tazila, who claimed to defend God's justice, are now accused of making God less good than His creatures.

?

But have you ever, even unintentionally, assumed that someone else's actions are 'better' than what God commands? For example, thinking a secular system produces better justice than Islamic law? Repentance begins with recognizing this attitude in ourselves.

Refutation of Thumama's View on Causation
Nasafi criticizes Thumama's view that effects can occur without an agent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Nasafi considers Thumama's view on causation to be a dangerous innovation that undermines the proof for God's existence.

Core Idea
Allowing effects without an agent destroys the very argument for a Creator.

Imam Nasafi here takes on a controversial view attributed to Thumama, a prominent Mu'tazili figure. This view claimed that precise and perfect actions could come into existence without a specifier or creator. Nasafi warns that this is not just a minor error but a wholesale negation of divine attributes—pure ta'til. Let's read his critique closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the literal translation to get the author's meaning.
Pay attention to the key terms.
2
Identify the core claim being refuted
Find Thumama's view as described by Nasafi: that many precise actions come into existence without a specifier or bringer into existence.
3
Understand the consequence
Nasafi says this view invalidates the method of proving the Maker. Why would that be? Because if effects can occur without a cause, the argument from design collapses.
4
Note the term 'ta'til'
The author calls this 'pure ta'til'—the complete denial of divine attributes. Recognize this as a severe accusation in Islamic theology.
Ta'til is often contrasted with tashbih (anthropomorphism).
5
Reflect on the author's response
Nasafi ends by seeking God's protection from uttering such a statement. This shows the gravity of the error in his view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لها، وأبطل بهذه البدعة على نفسه طريق إثبات الصانع حيث جوز أن كثيرا من الأفعال المحكمة المتقنة تخرج من العدم إلى الوجود وتختص بالوجود بعد العدم من غير تخصيص مخصص وإيجاد موجد، وهو التعطيل المحض – نسأل الله العصمة عن القول بمثله.
He invalidated by this innovation against himself the method of proving the Maker, where he permitted that many precise and perfect actions go out from non-existence into existence and become specified with existence after non-existence without specification by a specifier nor bringing into existence by a bringer-into-existence—and this is pure ta'til (negation of attributes). We ask God for protection from saying something similar.
Source pages p. 946

Commentary
This passage is a critique of the Mu'tazili figure Thumama's view on causation. The author (Imam Nasafi) states that Thumama's position effectively destroys the very argument for God's existence by allowing that complex actions can come into being without a specific agent. This is described as 'pure ta'til' – the complete denial of divine attributes and agency. The author then exclaims seeking God's protection from such a statement.

Key Terms

بدعة
إثبات الصانع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thumama's view is just a philosophical difference with no serious consequences.
Correction: Nasafi argues it undermines the entire proof for God's existence and constitutes pure ta'til (denial of divine attributes), making it a dangerous innovation.

Checkpoint
What does the author call Thumama's view that actions can exist without a specifier?
A) Pure innovation
B) Pure ta'til
C) Pure anthropomorphism
D) Pure determinism

Key Takeaway
Thumama's view that effects can occur without an agent is condemned as pure ta'til because it destroys the rational proof for God's existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever, in your daily life, act as if things happen without Allah's agency—like attributing success solely to your own effort? How does this lesson expose that as a subtle form of ta'til? What will you do today to consciously acknowledge Allah as the sole agent behind every outcome?
?
Nasafi seeks protection from uttering a statement that leads to ta'til. Are you careful with your words when discussing causality, or do you sometimes speak in a way that diminishes Allah's role? What specific phrase will you avoid from now on?
?
This passage shows that a seemingly 'intellectual' disagreement has catastrophic consequences for faith. Are you willing to examine your own beliefs about how things happen in the world, to ensure they do not undermine the proof for the Creator? What step will you take this week to strengthen your conviction that Allah is the only bringer-into-existence?

Mu'tazilite Scriptural Objections to Divine Will for Evil
Nasafi enumerates four scriptural objections of the Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four scriptural objections raised by the Mu'tazila against the Maturidi view that God wills all things, including evil.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila use Qur'anic verses to argue that God cannot will evil.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi begins presenting the doubts (shubah) of the Mu'tazila, which they use to oppose the belief that God wills all things. He first lists their scriptural objections—verses from the Qur'an that they claim show God does not will disbelief or hardship. Understanding these objections is crucial for appreciating the Maturidi response that follows.

Guided Path
1
Read the scriptural objections
Carefully read the Arabic passage listing four verses. Notice how the Mu'tazila interpret each verse to deny that God wills evil.
These are not the author's own views; they are the opponents' arguments.
2
Identify the four verses
Find each verse: creation for worship, ease and hardship, polytheists' claim, and no desire for injustice. Understand the Mu'tazilite inference from each.
3
Reflect on the challenge
Consider why these verses pose a problem for the Maturidi position. What response might a Maturidi give?
This prepares you for the subsequent rebuttal.

[شبه المعتزلة] فنقول: إن المعتزلة يتعلقون بشبه بعضها سمعية وبعضها عقلية. فأما السمعية فنحو قوله تعالى: (وَمَا خَلَقْتُ الْجِنَّ وَالْإِنسَ إِلَّا لِيَعْبُدُونِ) أخبر الله تعالى أنه خلقهم جميعًا للعبادة، وأنتم تقولون إنه خلق الكفرة منهم والعصاة لا للعبادة بل للكفر والمعصية. وقوله تعالى: (يُرِيدُ اللَّهُ بِكُمُ الْيُسْرَ وَلَا يُرِيدُ بِكُمُ الْعُسْرَ) والكفر أعسر العسر. وقوله تعالى: (سَيَقُولُ الَّذِينَ أَشْرَكُوا لَوْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ مَا أَشْرَكْنَا). فالله تعالى أخبر أنهم يقولون: لو شاء الله ما أشركنا ثم كذبهم في ذلك ورد قولهم بقوله: (كَذَلِكَ كَذَّبَ الَّذِينَ مِن قَبْلِهِمْ) وقوله: (كَذَلِكَ فَعَلَ الَّذِينَ مِن قَبْلِهِمْ) وأنتم تساعدون في المقالة من كذبه الله تعالى بنص كتابه وهو باطل. وقوله: (وَمَا اللَّهُ يُرِيدُ ظُلْمًا لِلْعِبَادِ) وعندكم يريد كل ظلم كان ويكون، وهو خلاف ما في الكتاب، وإكذاب الله تعالى في ما أخبر. وأما العقلية فكقولهم: مريد السفه سفيه اعتبارًا بالشاهد، ومريد الكفر كافر ومريد المعصية عاصي ويعتبر بالشاهد، ومريد شتم نفسه والافتراء عليه سفيه أيضا في الشاهد فكذا في الغائب إذ الشاهد دليل الغائب، ولأن العبد لا يمكنه
[Doubts of the Mu'tazila] So we say: Indeed, the Mu'tazila rely on doubts, some of which are scriptural and some rational. As for the scriptural, it is like His statement: 'And I did not create the jinn and mankind except to worship Me.' Allah informed that He created all of them for worship, but you say that He created the disbelievers and the disobedient from them not for worship but for disbelief and disobedience. And His statement: 'Allah desires ease for you and does not desire hardship for you' – and disbelief is the greatest hardship. And His statement: 'Those who associate partners will say: If Allah had willed, we would not have associated partners.' So Allah informed that they say: If Allah had willed, we would not have associated partners, then He belied them in that and rejected their statement by His saying: 'Thus did those before them deny' and His saying: 'Thus did those before them do.' And you assist in the statement of one whom Allah belied by the text of His Book, and that is false. And His statement: 'And Allah does not desire injustice for the servants' – and according to you, He desires every injustice that was and will be, and that is contrary to what is in the Book, and it is belying Allah in what He informed. As for the rational, it is like their statement: The one who wills foolishness is a fool, by analogy with the witnessed world; and the one who wills disbelief is a disbeliever, and the one who wills disobedience is a disobedient, and it is considered by analogy with the witnessed world; and the one who wills reviling of himself and slander against himself is also a fool in the witnessed world, so likewise in the unseen, because the witnessed world is an evidence for the unseen. And because the servant cannot...
Source pages p. 959

Commentary
This passage presents the Mu'tazilite objections against the Ash'ari/Maturidi position that God wills all things, including evil. The author first states that their doubts are of two types: scriptural (sam'iyya) and rational ('aqliyya). Then he lists four scriptural objections: (1) The verse of creation for worship (51:56) implies all are created for worship, contradicting the claim that some are created for disbelief. (2) The verse of ease and hardship (2:185) implies God does not will hardship, but disbelief is the greatest hardship. (3) The verse about polytheists saying 'If Allah had willed we would not have associated partners' (6:148) shows that God belied them, implying He did not will their shirk. (4) The verse 'Allah does not desire injustice for the servants' (40:31) contradicts the claim that He desires every injustice. The Mu'tazila argue that those who hold that God wills disbelief, disobedience, and injustice are attributing to God what He has denied and thus are belying Him. Then the passage turns to rational objections: by analogy (qiyas) with the witnessed world (al-shahid), the one who wills foolishness is foolish, the one who wills disbelief is a disbeliever, the one who wills disobedience is a disobedient, and the one who wills self-reviling is foolish. Therefore, if God wills these, He would be characterized by these negative attributes. The argument is based on the principle that the witnessed world is an evidence for the unseen (al-gha'ib). The rational objections continue with an incomplete statement about the servant not being able to... (the text ends).

شبه (shubah)
سمعية (sam'iyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These objections represent the Maturidi position.
Correction: These objections are presented as the Mu'tazilite argument, not the author's own view.

D) 'Say: He is Allah, the One'

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila use four Qur'anic verses to argue that God cannot will evil, challenging the Maturidi doctrine of universal divine will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Mu'tazila argue that God cannot will evil because He declares He does not desire injustice. Have you ever found yourself questioning God's will when faced with personal tragedy or injustice? How does recognizing the scriptural basis of this challenge affect your trust in God's wisdom?
?
When you read the verse 'I created jinn and mankind only to worship Me,' do you feel a tension between God's purpose for creation and the reality of widespread disbelief? How might you reconcile this while still affirming God's absolute will?
?
The polytheists claimed that God willed their shirk, and the Qur'an rejected their claim. Have you ever misused the concept of divine will to justify your own shortcomings? What would it mean for you to truly accept that God's will is beyond full human comprehension?

Mu'tazilite Rational Objections to Divine Will for Evil
Nasafi presents the Mu'tazilite rational objections based on analogy from the witnessed world.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational objections raised by the Mu'tazila against the Maturidi view that God wills all things, including evil, based on analogy with the witnessed world.

Core Idea
By analogy with human behavior, willing evil makes one evil; therefore, God cannot will evil.

After presenting scriptural objections, Imam al-Nasafi turns to the rational arguments of the Mu'tazila. They use qiyas (analogy) from the witnessed world (al-shahid) to the unseen (al-gha'ib): if a human who wills foolishness is called foolish, then if God wills foolishness, He would be foolish—impossible for God. This lesson examines that reasoning and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the rational objections
Read the Arabic passage on rational objections. Notice the analogy (i'tibar bi al-shahid) used repeatedly.
The argument is cut off, but the pattern is clear.
2
Understand the analogy
The Mu'tazila argue that in the witnessed world, willing a bad act makes one blameworthy. They then apply this to God by analogy, concluding that if God willed evil, He would be subject to the same judgment.
3
Identify the specific examples
Find the examples: willing foolishness, disbelief, disobedience, and self-reviling. Each is used to show that willing such acts would imply a flaw in the willer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

?

Will you submit your reasoning to God's inscrutable will?
?
The Mu'tazila used human analogy to defend God's perfection, but Ash'arites argue this anthropomorphizes God. Which approach resonates with your heart? When your mind cannot reconcile suffering with God's goodness, do you cling to the conviction that He is all-wise, or do you allow doubt to creep in? Make a decision today to trust God's wisdom even when you cannot see it.

Refutation of al-Ka'bi on Guidance and Misguidance
Nasafi refutes al-Ka'bi's interpretation of Q. 6:125.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi refutes al-Ka'bi by pointing out the inversion of cause and effect in the interpretation of Q. 6:125.

Core Idea
Al-Ka'bi reversed cause and effect; Nasafi restores the divine act as the cause of faith.

In this passage, Nasafi takes on al-Ka'bi's attempt to interpret the verse about the expanded heart as a post-act reward or punishment. He argues that this is a distortion of the Quranic wording, because the verse itself presents the expansion and constriction as the causes of faith and disbelief, not their consequences. We'll see how Nasafi unpacks this logical inversion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the structure of Nasafi's argument.
2
Identify al-Ka'bi's claim
Find the part where Nasafi quotes al-Ka'bi's interpretation. What does al-Ka'bi think the verse means?
Al-Ka'bi says the expansion/constriction is a reward/punishment.
3
Understand Nasafi's objection
Why does Nasafi call it tahrif? He points out that the verse attributes Islam to expansion, not the reverse. Show the cause-effect inversion.
The Quranic order: expansion → Islam. Al-Ka'bi reversed it.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider how this refutation defends the doctrine of divine causal power in guidance and misguidance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والكعبي لتحيره اعترض بما كانت المداواة أولى به لو كان ظن هذا الاعتراض صحيحًا فقال : معنى الآية أن من أسلم آتاه الله من لطائف ما لا يقدر عليه غيره ثوابًا لطاعته، ومن كفر ضيق الله صدره عقابًا لذلك، وهو تحريف للكتاب ونقل للكلم عن مواضعها وليس بتأويل وذلك لأن الله تعالى أثبت له الإسلام إذا شرح صدره، والكفر إذا صير قلبه ضيقًا حرجًا ولم يوجب شرح القلب لأنه أسلم، ولا ضيق القلب لأنه لم يؤمن، فكان ما قاله جعل ما هو جار مجرى الحكم علة، وجعل ما هو جار مجرى العلة حكما وفساده لا يخفى
And al-Ka'bi, due to his confusion, objected with what was more deserving of cure if his assumption of this objection were correct. He said: 'The meaning of the verse is that whoever submits, God gives him of the subtle things that none other can give as a reward for his obedience, and whoever disbelieves, God constricts his chest as a punishment for that.' This is a distortion of the Book and a displacement of words from their places, and it is not interpretation. This is because God Almighty established Islam for him when He expanded his chest, and disbelief when He made his heart narrow and constricted. He did not make the expansion of the heart because he submitted, nor the constriction of the heart because he did not believe. So what he said made what is in the position of the effect a cause, and made what is in the position of the cause an effect, and its corruption is not hidden.
Source pages p. 962

Commentary
This passage refutes al-Ka'bi's interpretation of the verse 'Whomever God wills to guide, He expands his breast to Islam' (Quran 6:125). Al-Ka'bi argued that the expansion or constriction is a reward or punishment that occurs after the act of faith or disbelief. Nasafi points out that this is a distortion (tahrif) and a displacement of words from their proper places, not a genuine interpretation (ta'wil). He explains that the verse itself attributes Islam to the expansion of the chest, and disbelief to the constriction, not the other way around. The expansion and constriction are the divine acts that cause faith or disbelief, not the consequences. Thus, al-Ka'bi inverted the cause and effect: he made what is actually the cause (the divine act) into an effect (reward/punishment), and made what is actually the effect (faith/disbelief) into a cause. Nasafi concludes that the corruption of this reasoning is obvious.

Key Terms
الهداية
الإضلال
شرح الصدر
ضيق الصدر
تحريف
تأويل
علة
حكم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's guidance or misguidance is a reward or punishment that occurs after a person's own choice of faith or disbelief.
Correction: Nasafi shows that the verse presents the divine act of expanding or constricting the chest as the cause that leads to faith or disbelief, not a consequence of it.

Checkpoint
What does Nasafi accuse al-Ka'bi of doing in his interpretation of the verse?
A) Reversing the cause and effect
B) Denying the verse altogether
C) Adding words not in the Quran
D) Ignoring the context

Key Takeaway
Al-Ka'bi's interpretation of the expanded heart verse inverts the causal relationship: the divine act is the cause of faith, not its reward.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience a moment of clarity or increased faith, do you tend to think it is because of your own righteousness or because God has chosen to expand your heart? How does this lesson's insistence that divine action is the cause reshape your understanding of gratitude and dependence on Him?
?
If God's expansion is the cause of faith, then what right do you have to look down on those who are not guided? Are you not in constant need of His continued expansion, and how does this realization affect your attitude toward others?

Refuting the Basran Mu'tazilite View on Guidance and Misguidance
Nasafi refutes the Basran Mu'tazilite interpretation of guidance and misguidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Basran Mu'tazilite interpretation that guidance is only explanation and misguidance only naming leads to logical absurdities and is therefore corrupt.

Core Idea
True guidance is more than explanation; it is a divine illumination that not all receive.

The Basran Mu'tazilites attempted to reduce God's guidance and misguidance to mere explanation and labeling. However, Imam Nasafi demonstrates that this interpretation collapses under its own logical weight. By examining the consequences of their claim, we see that it would make all people equally guided, contradicting the clear Quranic division between believers and disbelievers. This lesson walks through Nasafi's crisp refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let Nasafi's argument unfold naturally.
Notice the conditional structure: 'if... then...'.
2
Identify the hypothetical argument
Nasafi sets up a conditional: if expansion of the chest is merely receiving explanation, and explanation occurs for everyone, then everyone would have an expanded chest. Identify this chain.
This is the core of the refutation.
3
Understand the absurd conclusion
If the Basran view were true, disbelievers would simultaneously have expanded chests (due to receiving explanation) and constricted chests (due to being named misguided). Recognise why this is impossible.
This contradiction shows the view is false.
4
Reflect on the implication for God's division
Nasafi points out that the Quranic division between those with expanded chests and those with constricted chests would be baseless if everyone had an expanded chest. Consider why attributing error to God is kufr.
This strengthens the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعتراض البصريين أنه أراد بالهداية البيان وبالإضلال التسمية فاسد جدًا، لأن شرح الصدر لو كان يقع للبيان والبيان واقع للكل، لكان كل من وقع له البيان وقع له شرح الصدر، فكان كل كافر مشروح الصدر لحصول البيان له، ولكان يقع له ولكان يقع ضيق الصدر لتسميته تعالى إياه ضالاً، فكان كل كافر مشروح الصدر لحصول البيان له، ضيق الصدر لتسميته تعالى إياه ضالاً وهو محال، وكذا قسمة الله تعالى الخلق إلى من شرح له الصدر ، وإلى من جعل صدره ضيقًا باطلة إذ كل لما كان البيان واقعا وكان شرح الصدر له حاصلاً لم يبق أحد ليس بمشروح الصدر البتة، ونسبة الله تعالى إلى الخطأ فى القسمة كفر وضلال، وبالله العصمة.
And the objection of the Basrans that He meant by guidance explanation and by misguidance naming is very corrupt. Because if the expansion of the chest were for explanation, and explanation occurs for everyone, then everyone for whom explanation occurs would have expansion of the chest. So every disbeliever would have an expanded chest due to the occurrence of explanation for him, and constriction of the chest would occur for him due to His naming him as misguided. So every disbeliever would be expanded in chest for the occurrence of explanation for him, constricted in chest for His naming him misguided, which is impossible. Likewise, God's division of creation into those whose chest He expanded and those whose chest He made constricted would be false, since if explanation occurred and expansion of the chest was obtained for everyone, then there would remain no one at all without an expanded chest. Attributing error to God in the division is disbelief and misguidance. And with God is protection.
Source pages p. 962

Commentary
This passage refutes the Basran Mu'tazilite interpretation that God's guidance is merely explanation (bayan) of the truth, and misguidance is merely naming (tasmiya) someone as misguided. Nasafi argues that this interpretation leads to absurd consequences. If 'expansion of the chest' refers to receiving explanation, then since explanation is universal (all humans receive it), every disbeliever would also have an expanded chest. But the verse contrasts those with expanded chests and those with constricted chests. Thus, every disbeliever would simultaneously have an expanded chest (due to receiving explanation) and a constricted chest (due to being named misguided), which is contradictory. Furthermore, God's division of people into two groups would be invalid, because if everyone receives explanation and thus has an expanded chest, then no one would have a constricted chest. Accusing God of making an erroneous division is kufr and dalal. Thus, the Basran interpretation is corrupt.

Key Terms
البيان (explanation)
التسمية (naming)
شرح الصدر (expansion)
ضيق الصدر (constriction)
قسمة (division)
محال (impossible)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Guidance is only explanation and misguidance only naming.
Correction: True guidance involves a special divine illumination, as shown by the Quranic distinction between believers and disbelievers; mere explanation is insufficient.

Checkpoint
What logical problem does Nasafi find with the Basran interpretation that guidance is only explanation?
A) It would make disbelievers have both expanded and constricted chests
B) It denies that God guides anyone
C) It contradicts the literal meaning of the word
D) It is not based on any Quranic evidence

Key Takeaway
The Basran Mu'tazilite reduction of guidance to explanation collapses because it would make all people equally guided, contradicting the Quranic reality of belief and disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever thought that hearing the truth is enough for guidance? This passage shows that explanation alone does not expand the chest. Look at your own heart: Is your faith merely intellectual agreement, or has Allah truly opened your chest to embrace it? What would you say if He asked you why you believe?
?
When you encounter people who reject the message despite clear evidence, do you ever feel that God's guidance is unfair or ineffective? Nasafi warns that attributing error to God is disbelief. Examine your thoughts: Do you secretly doubt that God guides whom He wills? Repent from such thoughts and submit to His decree.
?
The Basran claim collapses because it makes all people equally guided. But you know that you were not always guided. What was the moment when your chest expanded to accept Islam? Was it just from hearing facts, or was it a divine opening? Thank Allah for that gift, and ask Him to keep your chest expanded until you meet Him.

Refuting Mu'tazila Interpretations of Divine Will
The author refutes Mu'tazila interpretations of divine will verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Maturidi author rejects Mu'tazila reinterpretations of Quranic verses about divine will, highlighting the logical and theological weaknesses in their approach.

Core Idea
Mu'tazila forced reinterpretations of divine will verses collapse under their own logical contradictions.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi confronts Mu'tazila attempts to reinterpret verses that clearly attribute will to Allah. He exposes the flaws in their reasoning, showing that their interpretations lead to absurdities. We will read his refutation and grasp the key points of his critique.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm and critique come through before you interpret.
Notice the author's use of Quranic quotes and sarcastic tone.
2
Identify the main arguments
Find the different points the author makes: the interpretation of 'yughwikum', the dilemma with al-Jubba'i, the criticism of 'Abd al-Jabbar, and the refutation of 'fitnah' interpretation.
3
Understand the logical dilemma
Focus on the author's question: does God want to punish them while willing disbelief from them or while willing faith? Either way leads to contradiction. This is the core of the refutation.
This shows that Mu'tazila interpretations cannot consistently explain God's will.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that the Mu'tazila objections are corrupt and anyone with minimal knowledge can see their falseness. Ask yourself why the author finds these interpretations so obviously wrong.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غيرهم أن المراد بقوله: ﴿ يُرِيدُ أَن يُغْوِيَكُمْ ﴾ أي يعاقبكم، وألغى يذكر ويراد به العذاب. قال الله تعالى: ﴿ فَسَوْفَ يَلْقَوْنَ غَيّا ) أي عذابا . وجوابه كجواب تأويل الجبائي أنه يريد أن يعاقبهم وهو يريد منهم الكفر أَوَيرِيدُ أن يعاقبهم وهو يريد منهم الإيمان؟ فبأي الجوابين أجاب فالكلام على ما ذكرنا ذكر هذه الوجوه وحكى كل تأويل عن صاحبه (۲) عبد الجبار الرازي(۳) ثم قال : وكل هذا واضح. فإن أراد أنه واضح وجه بطلانه فهو كما أراد، وإن أراد أنه واضح وجه صحته فهو يقول بقول يجب به الاستحياء من الناس (٤) والاستغفار من الله تعالى، والتعجب من رجل يدعي الترأس على أهل نحلته والتبحر في علوم أصحابه. ثم يرضى بمثل هذه التأويلات مع وهائها وظهور فسادها لأول الفكرة، وما أصدق ما قيل: حبك الشيء يعمي ويصم . وقال الله تعالى: ﴿ وَمَن يُرِدِ اللهُ فِتْنَتَهُ، فَلَن تَمْلِك لَهُ مِنَ اللَّهِ شَيْئًا () قيل: فتنته أي عذابه وقيل امتحانه بالرجم والقتل وإرادة ذلك بدون إرادة ما يستوجب به إرادة ظلم وتأويلهم أن قوله تعالى: "فتنته" أي تكليفه وامتحانه خطأ، لأن النبي عليه السلام ما كان يشق عليه ذلك، وما كان يسأل أن لا يكلف الله تعالى عباده وقال تعالى : ( أَوْلَتَيكَ الَّذِينَ لَمْ يُرِدِ اللهُ أَن يُطْهَرَ قُلُوبَهُمْ ) (٢). وعند المعتزلة أراد ذلك وفي الآيات كثرة ، ولهم اعتراضات عليها فاسدة لا معنى للاشتغال بذلك لوقوف من له أدنى علم على بطلان تلك الاعتراضات، وقال تعالى: ﴿ فَلَوْ شَاءَ لَهَدَنكُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ ) (۱) وقال تعالى: وَلَوْ شَاءَ رَبُّكَ لَآمَنَ مَن فِي الْأَرْضِ كُلُهُمْ جَمِيعًا ) (٢) وقال: وَلَوْ شَاءَ اللهُ مَا أَشْتَرَكُوا ) (۳).
Others [say] that the meaning of His saying: "He wants to lead you astray" is that He wants to punish you, and "ghayy" is mentioned and intended as punishment. Allah Almighty said: "Then they will encounter ghayy" i.e., punishment. Its answer is like the answer of the interpretation of al-Jubba'i: that He wants to punish them while He wants disbelief from them, or does He want to punish them while He wants faith from them? Whichever of the two answers he gives, the speech is as we mentioned: he mentioned these aspects and narrated each interpretation from its author (2) 'Abd al-Jabbar al-Razi (3), then said: All this is clear. If he means that the aspect of its falseness is clear, then it is as he meant; but if he means that the aspect of its correctness is clear, then he says a saying which necessitates shame before people (4) and seeking forgiveness from Allah Almighty, and wonder at a man who claims leadership over the people of his sect and mastery in the sciences of his companions, then is satisfied with such interpretations despite their weakness and the appearance of their corruption at first thought. How true is the saying: Love of something blinds and deafens. And Allah Almighty said: "Whomever Allah wants to test, you will not have [power] over him from Allah in anything" (5). It was said: His test means His punishment, or trial by stoning and killing, and willing that without willing what necessitates it is willing injustice. Their interpretation that His saying: "His test" means His obligation and trial is wrong, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) was not distressed by that, nor did he ask that Allah not oblige His servants. And He said: "Those are the ones for whom Allah did not want to purify their hearts" (2). According to the Mu'tazila, He wanted that, and there are many verses. They have corrupt objections to them, no need to occupy oneself with them, since anyone with minimal knowledge knows the falseness of those objections. And Allah said: "Had He willed, He would have guided you all" (1), and said: "Had your Lord willed, everyone on earth would have believed, all of them" (2), and said: "Had Allah willed, they would not have associated [partners]" (3).
Source pages p. 966

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Mu'tazila interpretations of several Quranic verses, in which the author (Imam al-Nasafi) criticizes their forced exegesis. The discussion begins by addressing the claim that the word 'yughwikum' (lead astray) actually means 'punish', and that 'ghayy' (error) means 'punishment'. The author then compares this to the interpretation of al-Jubba'i, pointing out a logical dilemma: if God intends to punish the disbelievers while also intending disbelief from them, or while intending faith from them, both alternatives lead to absurdities. He notes that 'Abd al-Jabbar al-Razi claimed that all this is clear, but the author retorts: if by 'clear' he means the falsity of the interpretation, then yes; if he means its correctness, then this is shameful and requires repentance. The author expresses astonishment that a scholar claiming leadership and knowledge could be satisfied with such weak and obviously corrupt interpretations. He then cites verses about 'fitnah' (trial) and argues that Mu'tazila explanations (like trial by stoning or obligation) are wrong because the Prophet was not distressed by God's commands. Further verses about God's will are quoted to argue that if God had willed, He would have guided all, but He did not; this contradicts Mu'tazila positions. The author concludes that the Mu'tazila have numerous corrupt objections but anyone with minimal knowledge knows they are false, so there is no need to engage them.

Key Terms
المشيئة
التأويل
الغيّ
الفتنة
الجبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila believe that verses about God's will can be reinterpreted to mean coercion or punishment rather than divine decree.
Correction: The author shows that such reinterpretations lead to logical contradictions and are clearly corrupt, as they conflict with the plain meaning of the verses and sound reason.

Checkpoint
What is the author's primary criticism of the Mu'tazila interpretations discussed in this passage?
A) They are too literal and fail to see deeper meanings.
B) They force interpretations that are weak and obviously corrupt, leading to logical absurdities.
C) They deny the Quran's clear meaning entirely.
D) They ignore the consensus of the early Muslims.

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi refutation demonstrates that Mu'tazila forced interpretations of divine will verses are logically inconsistent and theologically unsound.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson exposes how love for one's sect can blind a person to the truth. Is there any belief or practice you hold dear that, if you examined it honestly, you fear might be a comfortable illusion? What would it cost you to let go of that comfort for the sake of truth?
?
When you read the verse 'He wants to lead you astray,' does it stir unease in your heart about God's justice? How does the author's refutation remove that unease? Are you willing to submit to God's decree even when it challenges your sense of fairness?
?
The Prophet did not ask God to remove obligations. Think of the most difficult Islamic practice you face. Do you secretly wish it were easier or removed? What does your heart's posture toward that obligation reveal about your trust in God's wisdom?

The Consensus of the Ummah on Divine Will
Nasafi cites the consensus of the Ummah on the saying 'ما شاء الله كان'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the consensus of the Ummah on the saying 'ما شاء الله كان' serves as a definitive proof for the Maturidi position on divine will.

Core Idea
The Ummah's consensus on a theological principle is a certain proof of its truth.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi appeals to the consensus (ijma') of the Muslim community as a source of certain knowledge. The widely known phrase 'ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن' reflects the universal belief of Muslims, and any deviation from it is clearly erroneous. Let's examine how he establishes this consensus and its logical force.

Guided Path
1
Read the consensus passage
Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation. Notice how Nasafi presents the saying of the Ummah as a fixed statement without any doubt.
2
Identify the claim
What exactly is the saying of the Ummah? Why does Nasafi say it indicates the belief of all Muslims?
The phrase 'ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن' is the key.
3
Understand consensus as proof
Nasafi argues that consensus is a proof that gives certain knowledge. Why does he consider opposition to this consensus as clearly erroneous?
Consensus (ijma') is a source of certainty in Islamic theology.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Think about the strength of this argument. How does knowing that all Muslims have agreed on this phrase strengthen the Maturidi position?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قول الأمة: ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن من غير اضطراب قلب أحد دل أن اعتقاد جميع المسلمين أولاً وآخراً ما ذهبنا إليه، وقولهم مخالف لإجماع المسلمين وهو حجة موجبة للعلم بقطع القول على خطأ من خالفهم، ومعارضة الكعبي هذا بقول المسلمين ما أحب الله تعالى كان وما لم يحب لم يكن معارضة بما هو تقول على المسلمين وتخرص إذ لم يسمع أحد، ومعارضته لقول المسلمين أمر الله نافذ وكم من أمر لم يؤتمر معارضة فاسدة، لأن المراد بقولهم أمر الله نافذ أن أراد به أمر تكوين فهو مما له نفاذ، ولا يتصور أن لا ينفذ، فهذا والمشيئة سواء وإن أريد به أمر إيجاب وتكليف فحكمة وجوب الائتمار لا وجوده.
Then the saying of the Ummah: 'What Allah wills is, and what He does not will is not' without any disturbance of heart indicates that the belief of all Muslims, first and last, is what we have adopted. And their saying contradicts the consensus of the Muslims, and consensus is a proof that necessitates knowledge with certainty of the error of those who oppose them. And Ka'bi's opposition to this by the saying of the Muslims 'What Allah loves is, and what He does not love is not' is an opposition by that which is a fabrication against the Muslims and a false claim, for no one has heard this. And his opposition to the saying of the Muslims 'The command of Allah is executing' despite many commands not being obeyed is a corrupt opposition. Because the intended meaning of their saying 'The command of Allah is executing' is, if He intends by it the command of formation (takwin), then it is something that necessarily executes, and it is inconceivable that it does not execute. So this and the will are the same. And if He intends by it the command of obligation and duty, then its wisdom is the obligation of compliance, not its actual occurrence.
Source pages p. 973

Commentary
This passage appeals to the consensus (ijma') of the Muslim Ummah. The author states that the widely known saying 'ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن' (What Allah wills is, and what He does not will is not) reflects the belief of all Muslims from the beginning to the end, and this consensus is a proof that gives certain knowledge that those who oppose it are in error. The author then refutes the objection of Ka'bi, who allegedly claimed that Muslims say 'ما أحب الله كان وما لم يحب لم يكن' (What Allah loves is, and what He does not love is not). The author dismisses this as a fabrication, as no one has ever heard such a saying. Ka'bi also objects to the Muslim saying 'أمر الله نافذ' (The command of Allah is executing), noting that many commands are not obeyed. The author clarifies that if 'command' means the creative command (amr takwini), it always executes; if it means the legislative command (amr taklifi), it only requires the obligation to obey, not that obedience actually occurs. Thus, there is no contradiction.

Key Terms
قول الأمة
إجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what does the saying 'ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن' indicate?
A) That some Muslims doubt it
B) That the belief of all Muslims is what Nasafi and his school have adopted
C) That it is a weak hadith
D) That it is only an opinion of a few scholars

Key Takeaway
The consensus of the Ummah on the saying 'ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن' is a certain proof for the Maturidi position on divine will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'ما شاء الله كان' in daily life, do you truly believe it with your heart, or is it just a habit on your tongue? What would change if you lived as if every single event is exactly what Allah willed?
?
If the consensus of the Ummah is a certain proof, why do you sometimes doubt or follow minority opinions that contradict this consensus? Are you willing to submit your own reasoning to the overwhelming agreement of all Muslims across time?
?
Think of a recent disappointment or a situation that didn't go your way. Did you internally rebel against Allah's decree, or did you feel peace knowing 'ما لم يشأ لم يكن'? What step can you take today to truly accept that Allah's will is perfect, even when it hurts?

Refuting Ka'bi's Objections to Divine Will
Nasafi refutes Ka'bi's two objections about divine love and command.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi refutes Ka'bi's two objections regarding the sayings about divine love and command.

Core Idea
Ka'bi's objections are based on fabricated sayings and a misunderstanding of Allah's commands.

Imam Nasafi now addresses the objections raised by Ka'bi against the consensus view. Ka'bi tries to argue that Muslims also say 'ما أحب الله' and that not all divine commands are obeyed. Nasafi systematically dismantles these objections, showing they are either fabricated or misinterpreted.

Guided Path
1
Read Ka'bi's first objection
Read the passage about Ka'bi's claim that Muslims say 'ما أحب الله كان'. Understand Nasafi's response that this is a fabrication.
Nasafi says no one has heard this saying.
2
Read the second objection
Read about Ka'bi's argument that not all divine commands are obeyed, so the saying 'أمر الله نافذ' is contradicted.
This is about the apparent conflict.
3
Understand Nasafi's distinction
Nasafi distinguishes between the creative command (amr takwini) which always executes, and the legislative command (amr taklifi) which only obliges compliance.
This resolves the contradiction.

Why Guidance Is More Than Just Explanation: Refuting the Mu'tazilites
Author refutes Mu'tazilite views on guidance and misguidance using Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi proof that divine guidance (huda) is a created act, not merely explanation, based on Quranic verses that distinguish between teaching and true guidance.

Core Idea
Guidance is not just teaching; God alone creates true guidance in the heart.

The Mu'tazilites reduced divine guidance to mere explanation and invitation. But the Quran itself shows that even the Prophet could not guide whom he loved. This lesson unpacks that argument and shows why guidance must be a creative act of God.

Guided Path
1
Restate the Maturidi position
Note the opening claim: since God creates all actions, He is the real Guide and Misguider by creating the acts of guidance and misguidance.
This is the foundation of the argument.
2
Examine the first Quranic proof
Read Q. 28:56 and the author's reasoning: if guidance were only explanation, the Prophet would guide whom he loves. Since the verse denies that, guidance must be something beyond explanation.
3
Analyze the second proof from Q. 6:125
See how the author uses the verse about expansion of the breast. If guidance were only invitation, everyone invited would have an expanded breast, but that is false. This leads to an absurdity that would make the Quranic text false.
The author uses a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Apply the same logic to misguidance
Notice the parallel argument: if calling someone 'astray' were mere labeling, then everyone God names astray would have a constricted breast, which is not the case.
This completes the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونحن لما أقمنا الدلالة على أن الله تعالى خالق أفعال العباد كان هاديًا لتخليقه فعل الاهتداء، ومضلاً لتخليقه فعل الضلال ثم الذي يبطل جميع ما ذهبوا إليه من التأويلات قوله تعالى مخاطبًا لنبيه عليه السلام : إِنَّكَ لَا تَهْدِى مَنْ أَحْبَبْتَ وَلَكِنَّ اللَّهَ يَهْدِى مَن يَشَاءُ (٤) ولو كان الهدى هو البيان لكان النبي عليه السلام يهدي من أحبه ، فدل أن وراء البيان هداية أخرى وليس ذلك إلا ما قلنا يدل على أن الله تعالى (۹) قال : ( فَمَن يُرِدِ اللهُ أَن يَهْدِيَهُ يَشْرَحْ صَدْرَهُ لِلْإِسْلَامِ (1) ولو كان المراد من الهداية الدعوة وبيان الطريق ينبغي أن يقال كل من دعاه الله للإيمان وبين له طريق الدين فهو مشروح الصدر، فيصير قوله تعالى: (يَجْعَلْ صَدْرَهُ ضَيِّقًا حَرَجًا (1) باطلاً كذبًا وهو كفر، وكذا كل من يسميه الله تعالى ضالاً ينبغي أن يجعل صدره ضيقًا حرجًا وكذا كل من يجده ضالاً، ثم إن الله تعالى بين
And since we have established the proof that God Almighty is the creator of the actions of servants, He is the Guide (hādin) for His creation of the act of guidance, and the Misguider (muḍill) for His creation of the act of misguidance. Then that which invalidates all the interpretations they have adopted is the saying of God Almighty addressing His Prophet peace be upon him: 'Indeed, [O Muhammad], you do not guide whom you love, but Allah guides whom He wills' (4). And if guidance were merely explanation (bayān), the Prophet peace be upon him would guide whom he loves. So it indicates that beyond explanation there is another guidance, and that is nothing but what we have said—it indicates that God Almighty (9) said: 'So whoever Allah wants to guide, He expands his breast to [contain] Islam' (1). And if the intended meaning of guidance were the call and clarification of the path, it would be necessary to say that everyone whom God calls to faith and clarifies the path of religion to him is expanded of breast. Then the saying of God Almighty: 'He makes his breast tight and constricted' (1) would become false and a lie, and that is disbelief. Likewise, everyone whom God Almighty names 'astray' should have his breast made tight and constricted, and likewise everyone whom He finds astray. Then God Almighty clarified...
Source pages p. 991

Commentary
This passage provides a refutation of the Mu'tazilite interpretations regarding guidance (huda) and misguidance (dalal). The author first restates the Maturidi position: since God is the creator of all actions, including human acts of guidance and misguidance, He is properly called the Guide and the Misguider in a real sense. Then he presents the central proof that invalidates the Mu'tazilite view that guidance is merely explanation (bayān) or calling (da'wa). He cites Q. 28:56: 'Indeed, you do not guide whom you love, but Allah guides whom He wills.' If guidance were only teaching or clarification, the Prophet would be able to guide whomever he wanted. But the verse denies that, showing that there is a form of guidance beyond mere explanation. This other guidance is the creation of belief in the heart. Next, he uses Q. 6:125: 'So whoever Allah wants to guide, He expands his breast to [contain] Islam.' If guidance meant only invitation and clarification, then everyone God invites would have an expanded breast. But that is false, because many who hear the message remain stubborn. Therefore, if one insists that guidance is only explanation, then the verse about making the breast tight would be rendered false and even blasphemous. The author also applies the same logic to misguidance: if naming someone 'astray' were mere labeling, then everyone God names 'astray' should have a constricted breast, but that is not the case. Thus, the Mu'tazilite interpretations are invalidated.

Key Terms
الهدى
الضلال
البيان
شرح الصدر
خلق الأفعال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Mu'tazilites believe that 'guidance' (huda) is merely teaching and clarification (bayān) without any creative act from God.
Correction: The Quranic verses show that guidance is something God creates in the heart beyond mere explanation, because even the Prophet cannot guide by teaching alone.

Checkpoint
What does the author use as the main proof that guidance is more than just explanation (bayān)?
A) The verse 'So whoever Allah wants to guide, He expands his breast.'
B) The verse 'Indeed, [O Muhammad], you do not guide whom you love, but Allah guides whom He wills.'
C) The argument that God is the creator of all actions.
D) The linguistic analysis of the word 'huda'.

Key Takeaway
Guidance and misguidance are acts created by God, not merely explanations, as proven by Quranic verses that distinguish between teaching and actual guidance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a powerful sermon or read a verse, do you assume that simply understanding it is enough to change your heart? How does this lesson expose the danger of relying on your own comprehension rather than begging God for the act of guidance?
?
Think of a time you tried to guide someone—a friend or family member—with words and arguments, but they remained stubborn. Did you feel frustrated, perhaps thinking, 'I explained it so clearly'? How does Q.28:56 reframe your responsibility and redirect your hope?
?
The Mu'tazilites thought that calling people to faith was enough; God's part was just to send the message. Examine your own prayer life: do you truly ask God to expand your chest for Islam, or do you assume that because you have knowledge, you are already guided? What would change if you begged Him for that inner expansion today?

Refuting al-Jubba'i on Guidance
Nasafi refutes al-Jubba'i's claim that guidance means leading to Paradise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Jubba'i's interpretation of guidance as leading to Paradise is inconsistent with the Qur'anic text and the nature of divine will.

Core Idea
Allah's guidance is tied to His will, not a fixed rule of Paradise entrance.

Al-Jubba'i, a leading Mu'tazilite theologian, redefined the Qur'anic term 'guidance' (huda) as 'leading to Paradise in the afterlife'. This passage from Nasafi's Tabṣirat al-Adilla systematically refutes that claim using two key verses. Let's see how the argument unfolds.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal English translation without overthinking. Notice the key terms and the flow of the argument.
The passage begins by stating al-Jubba'i's interpretation is false.
2
Identify the two Qur'anic proofs
Nasafi quotes two verses to dismantle al-Jubba'i's position. Look for 'ulakinna Allaha yahdi man yasha'' and 'walaw shi'na laatayna kulla nafsin hudaha'. Understand how each verse contradicts the interpretation.
The first verse shows guidance is general; the second shows it would be universal if interpreted as Paradise.
3
Understand the rational inconsistency
Nasafi points out that if guidance meant Paradise, then Allah would only guide believers who die faithful, contradicting the generality of His will. Moreover, the second verse would imply everyone gets Paradise, which is impossible according to Mu'tazilite principles.
This shows that al-Jubba'i's interpretation fails both textually and rationally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتأويل الجبائي أنه هداية طريق الجنة في الآخرة باطل، لأنه تعالى قال: وَلَكِنَّ اللَّهَ يَهْدِي مَن يَشَاءُ والله لا يهدي طريق الجنة من شاء بل من مات على إيمانه، ثم عندهم لا يجوز أن لا يدخل الجنة من مات على إيمان ولم يرتكب الكبائر أو تاب عنها بعدما ارتكب ولو لم يدخل لصار ظالماً ولا يجوز له أن يدخل الجنة من كفر وارتكب كبيرة ومات قبل التوبة عنها فأي مشيئة في ذلك لله تعالى يدل عليه أنه تعالى قال: وَلَوْ شِئْنَا لَآتَيْنَا كُلَّ نَفْسٍ هُدَاهَا ولا يجوز صرفه إلى هداية طريق الجنة.
And al-Jubba'i's interpretation that it is guidance to the path of Paradise in the afterlife is false, because He Most High said: 'But Allah guides whom He wills'—and Allah does not guide to the path of Paradise whom He wills, but only those who die upon their faith. Then, according to them, it is not permissible that he who died upon faith and did not commit major sins or repented from them after committing them should not enter Paradise; if he did not enter, He would become unjust, and it is not permissible that he who disbelieved and committed a major sin and died before repentance from it should enter Paradise. So what will is there for Allah Most High in that? He indicates by His saying: 'And if We willed, We would have given every soul its guidance'—and it is not permissible to turn this to guidance to the path of Paradise.
Source pages p. 992

Commentary
This passage refutes the Mu'tazilite theologian al-Jubba'i's claim that the 'guidance' (huda) mentioned in the disputed verses refers to 'guidance to the path of Paradise in the afterlife'. The author argues that this interpretation is false for several reasons. First, the verse 'lakinna Allaha yahdi man yasha'' indicates generality: Allah guides whomever He wills, but if guidance meant leading to Paradise, then Allah would only guide believers who die in faith, not whomever He wills. Second, according to Mu'tazilite theology, whoever dies in faith without major sins must enter Paradise; otherwise God would be unjust. Similarly, a disbeliever who dies unrepentant cannot enter Paradise. Thus, there is no free will for Allah in such deterministic outcomes. Finally, the verse 'law shi'na laatayna kulla nafsin hudaha' (if We willed, We would give every soul its guidance) cannot be interpreted as guidance to Paradise, because that would require all people to be given Paradise, which is impossible by Mu'tazilite principles. Thus, al-Jubba'i's interpretation is inconsistent.

Key Terms
هداية
الجنة
الجبائي
المشيئة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Guidance in the Qur'an always means being led to Paradise in the afterlife.
Correction: Guidance is broader, tied to divine will, and cannot be reduced to a fixed eschatological outcome without contradicting other verses.

Checkpoint
Why does al-Jubba'i's interpretation of guidance as leading to Paradise fail according to this passage?
A) Because the Qur'an says guidance is only for believers
B) Because it limits Allah's will to a fixed outcome contradicting the general expression 'yahdi man yasha'
C) Because the Prophet said guidance means something else
D) Because the verse about giving every soul guidance would then be meaningless

Key Takeaway
Al-Jubba'i's interpretation of guidance as leading to Paradise is refuted by the unrestricted nature of divine will expressed in the Qur'an.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your guidance to faith is entirely by Allah's will, not by your own merit? How does that realization affect your humility before Him and your reliance on His mercy, especially when you see others who are not guided?
?
If you thought your good deeds guaranteed Paradise (like al-Jubba'i implies), would your fear of Allah decrease? This lesson shows that guidance is according to His will—does that make you more hopeful or more fearful? What does it call you to change in your heart?
?
When you read 'But Allah guides whom He wills,' are you content with that sovereignty? Or do you find yourself questioning why He guides some and not others? How can you submit to His will while still striving to call others to guidance?
